<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">List of Latin-script digraphs</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>
<div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
					Jump to:					<a href="#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="#p-search">search</a>
</div>
<div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td style="width:1px"></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters" title="Help:Special characters">special characters</a>.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/Help:Special_characters" title="Help:Special characters">rendering support</a>, you may see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a>.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>This is a <b>list of <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">digraphs</a></b> used in various <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabets</a>. Capitalization involves only the first letter (<i>ch</i> becomes <i>Ch</i>) unless otherwise stated (<i>ij</i> becomes <i>IJ</i>).</p>
<table class="metadata mbox-small noprint selfref" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;width: 22em;">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet"><img alt="[]" data-file-height="100" data-file-width="75" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/30px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/45px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Parentesi_Quadre.svg/60px-Parentesi_Quadre.svg.png 2x" width="30"/></a></td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="vertical-align:middle; font-size:95%;"><b>This article contains <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">IPA</a> phonetic symbols.</b> Without proper <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet#Fonts" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">rendering support</a>, you may see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Replacement_character" title="Replacement character">question marks, boxes, or other symbols</a> instead of <a href="/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> characters.</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Letters with diacritics are arranged in alphabetic order according to their base: ⟨å⟩ is alphabetized with ⟨a⟩, not at the end of the alphabet, as it would be in <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>. Substantially-modified letters, such as ⟨<a href="/wiki/S" title="S">ſ</a> ⟩ (a variant of ⟨s⟩) and ⟨ɔ⟩ (based on ⟨o⟩), are placed at the end.</p>
<div aria-labelledby="tocheading" class="toc plainlinks hlist" id="toc" role="navigation" style="text-align:left;">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Apostrophe">Apostrophe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Apostrophe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>’b</b>⟩ (capital ⟨<b>’B</b>⟩) is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bari_alphabet" title="Bari alphabet">Bari alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɓ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>’d</b>⟩ (capital ⟨<b>’D</b>⟩) is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bari_alphabet" title="Bari alphabet">Bari alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɗ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>’y</b>⟩ (capital ⟨<b>’Y</b>⟩) is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bari_alphabet" title="Bari alphabet">Bari alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔʲ/</span>. It is also used for this sound in the <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">Hausa language</a> in Nigeria, but in Niger, Hausa ⟨’y⟩ is replaced with ⟨ƴ ⟩.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="A">A</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: A">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>a’</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa</a> orthography, where it represents the <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> or <a href="/wiki/Creaky_voice" title="Creaky voice">creaky-voiced</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a̰/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>aa</b>⟩ is used in the orthographies of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_alphabet" title="Dutch alphabet">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finnish_orthography" title="Finnish orthography">Finnish</a> and other languages with phonemic long vowels for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aː/</span>. It was <a href="/wiki/Danish_and_Norwegian_alphabet#History" title="Danish and Norwegian alphabet">formerly used in Danish and Norwegian</a> (and still is in some proper names) for the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span>, now spelled ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C3%85" title="Å">å</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ae</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a>, where it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span> between two "broad" (<a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">velarized</a>) consonants, e.g. <i>Gael</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡˠeːlˠ/</span> ('a <a href="/wiki/Gaels" title="Gaels">Gael</a>').<br/></p>
<dl>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/Latin_spelling_and_pronunciation" title="Latin spelling and pronunciation">Latin orthography</a>, ⟨ae⟩ originally represented the <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ai/</span>, before it was <a href="/wiki/Monophthong" title="Monophthong">monophthongized</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Vulgar_Latin" title="Vulgar Latin">Vulgar Latin</a> period to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>; in medieval manuscripts, the digraph was frequently replaced by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligature_(typography)" title="Ligature (typography)">ligature</a> ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C3%86" title="Æ">æ</a>⟩.</dd>
<dd>In Modern English, Latin loanwords with ⟨ae⟩ are generally pronounced with <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> (e.g. <i>Caesar</i>), prompting <a href="/wiki/Noah_Webster" title="Noah Webster">Noah Webster</a> to shorten this to ⟨e⟩ in his 1806 <a href="/wiki/Spelling_reform" title="Spelling reform">spelling reform</a> for <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">American English</a>.</dd>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/German_orthography" title="German orthography">German orthography</a>, ⟨ae⟩ is a variant of ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C3%84" title="Ä">ä</a>⟩ found in some proper names or in contexts where ⟨ä⟩ is unavailable.</dd>
<dd>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_alphabet" title="Dutch alphabet">Dutch alphabet</a>, ⟨ae⟩ is an old spelling variant of the ⟨aa⟩ digraph but now only occurs in names of people or (less often) places and in a few loanwords from Greek.</dd>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">Zhuang</a>, ⟨ae⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> (⟨a⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aː/</span>).</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>ãe</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃ĩ̯/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ah</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa</a> orthography, where it represents the breathy or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a̤/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ai</b>⟩ is used in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>, typically representing the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, as a result of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Vowel_Shift" title="Great Vowel Shift">Great Vowel Shift</a>, the vowel of ⟨ai⟩ has shifted from this value to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> as in <i>pain</i> and <i>rain</i>, while it may have a sound of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> in unstressed syllables like <i>bargain</i> and <i>certain(ly)</i>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> in the stressed syllable of <i>again(st)</i> (AmE), depending on the word; while in <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, a different change, <i>monophthongization</i>, has occurred, resulting in the digraph representing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>. A similar change has also occurred during the <a href="/wiki/Koine_Greek_phonology#Diphthongs" title="Koine Greek phonology">development of Greek</a>, resulting in ⟨αι⟩ and the ⟨<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%CE%95" title="Ε">ε</a>⟩ both having the same sound; originally <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>, later <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/German_orthography" title="German orthography">German orthography</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span> as in <i>Kaiser</i> (which derived from Latin <i>caesar</i>). However, most German words use ⟨ei⟩ for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Kernowek_Standard" title="Kernowek Standard">Kernowek Standard</a> orthography of <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span>, mostly in loanwords from English such as <i>paint</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>aí</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>aî</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛː/</span>, as in <i>aînesse</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛːnɛs/</span> or <i>maître</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mɛːtʁ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ái</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ãi</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃ĩ̯/</span>. It has, thus, the same value as ⟨<b>ãe</b>⟩, but the latter is much more common.</p>
<p>⟨<b>am</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃ũ̯/</span> at the end of a word, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃/</span> before a consonant, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/am/</span> before a vowel; and in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑ̃/</span> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/am/</span> before a vowel).</p>
<p>⟨<b>âm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">stressed</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>an</b>⟩ is used in many languages to write a <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">nasal vowel</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃/</span> before a consonant, in French it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑ̃/</span>, and in many <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> languages it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ã/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ân</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Stress_(linguistics)" title="Stress (linguistics)">stressed</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>än</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetan_Pinyin" title="Tibetan Pinyin">Tibetan Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span>. It is alternately written ⟨<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ain_(trigraph)" title="Ain (trigraph)">ain</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ån</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Walloon_language" title="Walloon language">Walloon language</a>, for the nasal vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ̃/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>aŋ</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lakhota_language" title="Lakhota language">Lakhota</a> for the nasal vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ã/</span></p>
<p>⟨<b>ao</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span>, depending on dialect, between broad consonants. In <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a>, it is found in a few words such as <i>paonne</i> representing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span>, and in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/au̯/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Wymysorys_language" title="Wymysorys language">Vilamovian</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> (also spelt ⟨å⟩).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ão</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐ̃ũ̯/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>aq</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa</a> orthography, for the <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">pharyngealized</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aˤ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>au</b>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> is a result of various linguistic changes from Middle English, having shifted from <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">*/au/</span> to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔː/</span>. In a number of dialects, this has merged with <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑː/</span>. It occasionally represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aʊ/</span>, as in <i>flautist</i>. Other pronunciations are <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ/</span> in North American English <i>aunt</i> and <i>laugh</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> in <i>gauge</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> as in <i>gauche</i> and <i>chauffeur</i>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> as in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meerschaum" title="Meerschaum">meerschaum</a></i> and <i>restaurant</i>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, it is used for the diphthongs <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/au/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʌu/</span> respectively (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/au/</span> in some northern and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔu/</span> in some southern Dutch and some Flemish dialects).</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a>, ⟨au⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> or sometimes <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span>. It most frequently appears in the inflectional ending marking plurals of certain kinds of words like <i>cheval</i> ('horse') or <i>canal</i> ('channel'), respectively having a plural in <i>chev<b>au</b>x</i> and <i>can<b>au</b>x</i>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_orthography" title="Icelandic orthography">Icelandic orthography</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œy/</span>.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Kernowek_Standard" title="Kernowek Standard">Kernowek Standard</a> orthography of <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, ⟨au⟩ stands for long <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔː/</span> or short <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span>, as in <i>caul</i> ('cabbage') or <i>dauncya</i> ('to dance').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>äu</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/German_orthography" title="German orthography">German orthography</a> for the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔɪ/</span> in declension of native words with <i>au</i>; elsewhere, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔʏ/</span> is written as ⟨<b>eu</b>⟩. In words where ä|u is separated in two syllables, mostly of Latin origin, ⟨äu⟩ is pronounced as <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ.ʊ/</span>, as in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matth%C3%A4us_(disambiguation)" title="Matthäus (disambiguation)">Matthäus</a></i> (one German form for <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthew_(name)" title="Matthew (name)">Matthew</a></i>).</p>
<p>⟨<b>aû</b>⟩ was used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a> but has been replaced<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (December 2012)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup"><span title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">replaced by what?</span></a></i>]</sup>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>aw</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> in ways that parallel English ⟨au⟩, though it appears more often at the end of a word. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, ⟨aw⟩ represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aʊ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æʊ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Welsh_orthography" title="Welsh orthography">Welsh orthography</a>, ⟨aw⟩ represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/au/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ay</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> in ways that parallel English ⟨ai⟩, though it appears more often at the end of a word. Unlike ⟨ai⟩, ⟨ay⟩ functions almost the same as ⟨ey⟩ (the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i:/</span> sound in <i>key</i>) at the end of variant spellings of names like <i>Lindsay</i> and <i>Ramsay</i>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a>, it is usually used to represent /ɛj/ before a vowel (as in <i>ayant</i>) and /ɛ.i/ before a consonant (as in <i>pays</i>).</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, ⟨ay⟩ represents the sounds <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/əɪ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛː/</span>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-3"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="B">B</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: B">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>bb</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>, where <i>b</i> stands for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p/</span>. In English, doubling a letter indicates that the previous vowel is short (so <i>bb</i> represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>). In ISO romanized <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, it is used for the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p͈/</span>, otherwise spelled ⟨pp⟩; an example is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hobbang" title="Hobbang">hobbang</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is the rare ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʼ/</span>. In several African languages it is implosive <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɓ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>bd</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> in a few words of Greek origin, such as <i>bdellatomy.</i> When not initial, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bd/</span>, as in <i>abdicate.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>bh</b>⟩ is used in transcriptions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_language" title="Indo-Aryan language">Indo-Aryan languages</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_plosive" title="Voiced bilabial plosive">voiced bilabial plosive</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bʱ/</span>). In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a>, it stands for the <a href="/wiki/Phoneme" title="Phoneme">phonemes</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/vʲ/</span>, for example <span lang="ga" xml:lang="ga"><i>mo bhád</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mə waːd̪ˠ/</span> ('my boat'), <span lang="ga" xml:lang="ga"><i>bheadh</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/vʲɛx/</span> ('would be'). In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthography_for_languages_of_Guinea_(pre-1985)" title="Orthography for languages of Guinea (pre-1985)">orthography used in Guinea before 1985</a>, ⟨bh⟩ was used in <a href="/wiki/Pular_language" title="Pular language">Pular</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula language</a>) for the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_bilabial_implosive" title="Voiced bilabial implosive">voiced bilabial implosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɓ/</span>, whereas in <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a>, ⟨b⟩ represents the implosive and ⟨bh⟩ represents the plosive <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>bm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for an optionally <a href="/wiki/Pre-stopped_consonant" title="Pre-stopped consonant">pre-occluded</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span>; that is, it is pronounced either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mː/</span> (in any position); <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵇm/</span> (before a consonant or finally); or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bm/</span> (before a vowel); examples are <i>mabm</i> ('mother') or <i>hebma</i> ('this').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-4"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-2"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>bp</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_language" title="Sandawe language">Sandawe</a> and romanized <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p/</span>, and in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>bv</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_labiodental_affricate" title="Voiced labiodental affricate">voiced labiodental affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b̪͡v/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>bz</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona language</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whistled_sibilant" title="Whistled sibilant">whistled sibilant</a> cluster <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bz͎/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="C">C</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: C">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>cc</b>⟩ is used in Andean Spanish for loanwords from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a> or <a href="/wiki/Aymara_language" title="Aymara language">Aymara</a> with <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/q/</span>, as in <i>Ccozcco</i> (modern <i>Qusqu)</i> ('<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuzco" title="Cuzco">Cuzco</a>'). In many European languages, ⟨cc⟩ before <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">front vowels</a> represents a sequence such as <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ks/</span>, e.g. English <i>success</i>, French <i>occire</i>, Spanish <i>accidente</i> (dialectally <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ks/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kθ/</span>); this is not the case of <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, where a ⟨cc⟩ before a <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">front vowel</a> represents a geminated <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>, as in <i>lacci</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈlat.tʃi/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lombard_language" title="Lombard language">Lombard</a>, ⟨cc⟩ represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> sound at the end of a word. In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is the glottalized click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǀˀ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>cg</b>⟩ was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span> in Old English (<i>ecg</i> in Old English sounded like 'edge' in Modern English). It is used for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǀχ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a>, and in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_click" title="Voiceless dental click">voiceless dental click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǀ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Ch_(digraph)" title="Ch (digraph)">ch</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages. In English, it can represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span>. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>čh</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Romani_orthography" title="Romani orthography">Romani orthography</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Chechen_language" title="Chechen language">Chechen</a> Latin alphabet for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃʰ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet, it was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃʼ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ci</b>⟩ is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_alphabet" title="Italian alphabet">Italian alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> before the non-front vowel letters ⟨a, o, u⟩. In <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a>, it usually represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> whenever it precedes any vowel other than ⟨i⟩. In <a href="/wiki/Polish_orthography" title="Polish orthography">Polish orthography</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ɕ/</span> whenever it precedes a vowel, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ɕi/</span> whenever it precedes a consonant (or in the end of the word), and is considered a graphic variant of <a href="/wiki/%C4%86" title="Ć">ć</a> appearing in other situations.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ck</b>⟩ is used in many <a href="/wiki/Germanic_languages" title="Germanic languages">Germanic languages</a> in lieu of ⟨kk⟩ or ⟨cc⟩ to indicate either a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geminated" title="Geminated">geminated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kː/</span>, or a <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> with a preceding (historically) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Short_vowel" title="Short vowel">short vowel</a>. The latter is the case with English <i>tack</i>, <i>deck</i>, <i>pick</i>, <i>lock</i>, and <i>buck</i> (compare <i>backer</i> with <i>baker</i>). In <a href="/wiki/German_orthography" title="German orthography">German orthography</a>, ⟨ck⟩ indicates that the preceding vowel is short. Prior to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_spelling_reform_of_1996" title="German spelling reform of 1996">German spelling reform of 1996</a>, it was replaced by ⟨k-k⟩ for syllabification. The new spelling rules allow only syllabification of the ⟨ck⟩ as a whole:</p>
<dl>
<dd>
<ul>
<li>Old spelling: <i>Säcke</i>: <i>Säk-ke</i> ('sacks')</li>
<li>New spelling: <i>Säcke</i>: <i>Sä-cke</i></li>
</ul>
</dd>
<dd>Among the modern Germanic languages, ⟨ck⟩ is used mainly in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alsatian_language" title="Alsatian language">Alsatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Luxembourgish_language" title="Luxembourgish language">Luxembourgish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scots_language" title="Scots language">Scots</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>, and other <a href="/wiki/West_Germanic_languages" title="West Germanic languages">West Germanic languages</a> in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>. Similarly, ⟨kk⟩ is used for the same purpose in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" title="Afrikaans language">Afrikaans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a>, and other West Germanic languages in the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>. Compare the word <i>nickel</i>, which is the same in many of these languages except for the customary ⟨ck⟩ or ⟨kk⟩ spelling. The word is <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nickel" title="wiktionary:nickel">nickel</a></i> in English and Swedish, <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Nickel" title="wiktionary:Nickel">Nickel</a></i> in German, and <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/nikkel" title="wiktionary:nikkel">nikkel</a></i> in Afrikaans, Danish, Dutch, Icelandic and Norwegian.</dd>
<dd>It was also used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_click" title="Voiceless dental click">voiceless dental click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǀ/</span> (equivalent to ⟨cg⟩).</dd>
<dd>It is also used in <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> at the end of a syllable after a short vowel; only in loanwords (mostly from English) in the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Written_Form" title="Standard Written Form">Standard Written Form</a> (SWF),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> more widely in <a href="/wiki/Kernowek_Standard" title="Kernowek Standard">Kernowek Standard</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-5"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup></dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>cn</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> in a few words of Greek origin, such as <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cnidarian" title="Cnidarian">cnidarian</a>.</i> When not initial, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kn/</span>, as in <i>acne.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>cö</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Seri_language" title="Seri language">Seri</a> alphabet for a <a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">labialized</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_plosive" title="Voiceless velar plosive">velar plosive</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span>. It is placed between ⟨<a href="/wiki/C" title="C">C</a>⟩ and ⟨<a href="/wiki/E" title="E">E</a>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>cr</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʈʂ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>cs</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_alphabet" title="Hungarian alphabet">Hungarian alphabet</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless postalveolar affricate">voiceless postalveolar affricate</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>. It is considered a distinct letter, named <i>csé</i>, and is placed between ⟨<a href="/wiki/C" title="C">C</a>⟩ and ⟨<a href="/wiki/D" title="D">D</a>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>. Examples of words with cs include <i>csak</i> ('only'), <i>csésze</i> ('cup'), <i>cső</i> ('pipe').</p>
<p>⟨<b>ct</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span> in a few words of Greek origin, such as <i>ctenoid.</i> When not initial, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kt/</span>, as in <i>act</i>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>cu</b>⟩ is used in the orthographies for languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">Nahuatl</a> (that is, based on <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">Spanish</a> or <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a>) for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span>. In Nahuatl, ⟨cu⟩ is used before a vowel, whereas ⟨uc⟩ is used after a vowel.</p>
<p>⟨<b>cx</b>⟩ is used unofficially in lieu of <a href="/wiki/Esperanto_orthography" title="Esperanto orthography">Esperanto orthography</a>'s ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C4%88" title="Ĉ">ĉ</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>cz</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Polish_orthography" title="Polish orthography">Polish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ʂ/</span> as in <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-cze%C5%9B%C4%87.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Pl-cze%C5%9B%C4%87.ogg" title="Pl-cześć.ogg"><b>cz</b>eść</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Pl-cze%C5%9B%C4%87.ogg" title="File:Pl-cześć.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span> ('hello'). In <a href="/wiki/Kashubian_language" title="Kashubian language">Kashubian</a>, ⟨cz⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>. This digraph was once common across Europe (which explains the English spelling of <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Czech_(disambiguation)" title="Czech (disambiguation)">Czech</a>), but has largely been replaced. In <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, historical ⟨cz⟩ contracted to the <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">ligature</a> ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C3%87" title="Ç">ç</a>⟩, and represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, it was formerly used for the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ts/</span>, which is now written ⟨c⟩.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="D">D</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: D">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>dc</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a> for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᶢǀ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dd</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> to indicate a <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span> with a preceding (historically) short vowel (e.g. <i>jaded</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈdʒeɪdəd/</span> has a "long a" while <i>ladder</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈlædər/</span> has a "short a"). In <a href="/wiki/Welsh_orthography" title="Welsh orthography">Welsh orthography</a>, ⟨dd⟩ represents a <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_fricative" title="Voiced dental fricative">voiced dental fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ð/</span>. It is treated as a distinct letter, named <i>èdd</i>, and placed between ⟨<a href="/wiki/D" title="D">D</a>⟩ and ⟨<a href="/wiki/E" title="E">E</a>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>. In the ISO romanization of <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, it is used for the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͈/</span>, otherwise spelled ⟨tt⟩; examples are <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ddeokbokki" title="Ddeokbokki">ddeokbokki</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bindaeddeok" title="Bindaeddeok">bindaeddeok</a></i>. In the <a href="/wiki/Basque_alphabet" title="Basque alphabet">Basque alphabet</a>, it represents a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_plosive" title="Voiced palatal plosive">voiced palatal plosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɟ/</span>, as in <i>onddo</i>, ('mushroom'). In several African languages it is implosive <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɗ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dg</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span> in certain contexts, such as with <i>judgement</i> and <i>hedge</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>dh</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_alphabet" title="Albanian alphabet">Albanian alphabet</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swahili_alphabet" title="Swahili alphabet">Swahili alphabet</a>, and the orthography of the revived <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish language</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-6"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> for the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_fricative" title="Voiced dental fricative">voiced dental fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ð/</span>. The first examples of this digraph are from the <a href="/wiki/Oaths_of_Strasbourg" title="Oaths of Strasbourg">Oaths of Strasbourg</a>, the earliest French text, where it denotes the same sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ð/</span> developed mainly from intervocalic Latin -<i>t</i>-.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<dl>
<dd>In early traditional Cornish ⟨ȝ⟩ (<a href="/wiki/Yogh" title="Yogh">yogh</a>), and later ⟨th⟩, were used for this purpose. <a href="/wiki/Edward_Lhuyd" title="Edward Lhuyd">Edward Lhuyd</a> is credited for introducing the grapheme to Cornish orthography in 1707 in his <i>Archaeologia Britannica</i>. In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> it represents the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_fricative" title="Voiced velar fricative">voiced velar fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣ/</span> or the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_approximant" title="Voiced palatal approximant">voiced palatal approximant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span>; at the beginning of a word it shows the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">lenition</a> of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d̪ˠ/</span>, for example <i>mo dhoras</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mˠə ɣoɾˠəsˠ/</span> ('my door' cf. <i>doras</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d̪ˠorˠəsˠ/</span> 'door').</dd>
<dd>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthography_for_languages_of_Guinea_(pre-1985)" title="Orthography for languages of Guinea (pre-1985)">pre-1985 orthography of Guinea</a>, ⟨dh⟩ was used for the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolar_implosive" title="Voiced alveolar implosive">voiced alveolar implosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɗ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Pular_language" title="Pular language">Pular</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula language</a>. It is currently written ⟨ɗ⟩. In the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a> it is the opposite: ⟨dh⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>, and ⟨d⟩ <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɗ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a>, ⟨dh⟩ represents a dental stop, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t̪/</span>.</dd>
<dd>In addition, ⟨dh⟩ is used in various romanization systems. In transcriptions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_language" title="Indo-Aryan language">Indo-Aryan languages</a>, for example, it represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_plosive" title="Voiced dental plosive">voiced dental plosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d̪ʱ/</span> and in the <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanization of Arabic</a>, it denotes ⟨<span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%EF%BA%AB" title="ﺫ">ﺫ</a></span>⟩, which represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ð/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Modern_Standard_Arabic" title="Modern Standard Arabic">Modern Standard Arabic</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>dj</b>⟩ is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Faroese_alphabet" title="Faroese alphabet">Faroese</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> and many French-based orthographies for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a>, it represents a postalveolar stop such as <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ṯ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ḏ/</span>; this sound is also written ⟨dy⟩, ⟨tj⟩, ⟨ty⟩, or ⟨c⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dl</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong language</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tˡ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Navajo_language" title="Navajo language">Navajo language</a> orthography, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɬ/</span>, and in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɮ̈/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/cɬʼ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dł</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_alphabet" title="Tlingit alphabet">Tlingit alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɬ/</span> (in Alaska, ⟨dl⟩ is used instead).</p>
<p>⟨<b>dm</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nasal_release" title="Nasal release">nasally released</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡pn͡m/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dn</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Nasal_release" title="Nasal release">nasally released</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tn/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it is used for an optionally <a href="/wiki/Pre-stopped_consonant" title="Pre-stopped consonant">pre-occluded</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>; that is, it is pronounced either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nː/</span> (in any position); <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵈn/</span> (before a consonant or finally); or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dn/</span> (before a vowel); examples are <i>pedn</i> ('head') or <i>pednow</i> ('heads').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-7"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-4"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>dp</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡p/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dq</b>⟩ is used for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᶢǃ/</span> in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dr</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɖʐ/</span>. See ⟨<a href="#T">tr</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dt</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_language" title="Sandawe language">Sandawe</a> orthography as well as the romanization of <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dv</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_dental_affricate" title="Voiced dental affricate">voiced dental affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ð/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dx</b>⟩ is used in the orthographies of some <a href="/wiki/Zapotecan_languages" title="Zapotecan languages">Zapotecan languages</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">voiced postalveolar fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span>. It is placed between ⟨<a href="/wiki/D" title="D">D</a>⟩ and ⟨<a href="/wiki/E" title="E">E</a>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dy</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa language</a> orthography for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʲʱ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a> alphabet, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒɡ/</span>. It is the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a>, it represents a postalveolar stop such as <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ṯ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ḏ/</span>. This sound is also written ⟨tj⟩, ⟨dj⟩, ⟨ty⟩, ⟨c⟩, or ⟨j⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Dz_(digraph)" title="Dz (digraph)">dz</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages, often to represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡z/</span>. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>dź</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_alphabet" title="Polish alphabet">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorbian_alphabet" title="Sorbian alphabet">Sorbian</a> alphabets for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʑ/</span>, the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_affricate" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal affricate">voiced alveolo-palatal affricate</a>, as in <i>dźwięk</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʑvʲɛŋk/</span>. ⟨Dź⟩ is never written before a <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowel</a> (⟨dzi⟩ is used instead, as in <i>dziecko</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʑɛt͡skɔ/</span> 'child').</p>
<p>⟨<b>dż</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Polish_alphabet" title="Polish alphabet">Polish alphabet</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Voiced_retroflex_affricate" title="Voiced retroflex affricate">voiced retroflex affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʐ/</span> (e.g. <span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-d%C5%BCem.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9d/Pl-d%C5%BCem.ogg" title="Pl-dżem.ogg"><b>dż</b>em</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Pl-d%C5%BCem.ogg" title="File:Pl-dżem.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span> 'jam').</p>
<p>⟨<b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/D%C5%BE_(digraph)" title="Dž (digraph)">dž</a></b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">Serbo-Croatian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a> languages to represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʒ/</span>. See article.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E">E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>e′</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, where it represents the <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> or <a href="/wiki/Creaky_voice" title="Creaky voice">creaky</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ḛ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ea</b>⟩ is used in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a>, ⟨ea⟩ usually represents the monophthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> as in <i>meat</i>; due to a <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_high_front_vowels#Bred.E2.80.93bread_merger" title="Phonological history of English high front vowels">sound change</a> that happened in Middle English, it also often represents the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> as in <i>sweat</i>. Rare pronunciations occur, like <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> in just <i>break</i>, <i>great</i>, <i>steak</i>, and <i>yea</i>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ/</span> in the archaic <i><a href="/wiki/Ealdorman" title="Ealdorman">ealdorman</a></i>. When followed by <b>r</b>, it can represent the standard outcomes of the previously mentioned three vowels in this environment: <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪər/</span> as in <i>beard</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɜːr/</span> as in <i>heard</i>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛər/</span> as in <i>bear</i>, respectively; as another exception, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑr/</span> occurs in the words <i>hearken</i>, <i>heart</i> and <i>hearth</i>. It often represents two independent vowels, like <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ.ɑː/</span> (<i>seance</i>), <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i.æ/</span> (<i>reality</i>), <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i.eɪ/</span> (<i>create</i>), and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i.ɪ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i.ə/</span> (<i>lineage</i>). Unstressed, it may represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jə/</span> (<i>ocean</i>) and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> (<i>Eleanor</i>). In the <a href="/wiki/Romanian_alphabet" title="Romanian alphabet">Romanian alphabet</a>, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e̯a/</span> as in <i>beată</i> ('drunk female'). In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a>, ⟨ea⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/a/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant. In <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æɑ̯/</span>. ⟨Ea⟩ is also the transliteration of the ⟨<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%E1%9B%A0" title="ᛠ">ᛠ</a>⟩ rune of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Frisian_Futhorc" title="Anglo-Frisian Futhorc">Anglo-Frisian Futhorc</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>eá</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aː/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>éa</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ee</b>⟩ represents a long mid vowel in a number of languages. In <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a>, ⟨ee⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> as in <i>teen</i>. In both the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_alphabet" title="Dutch alphabet">Dutch</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_alphabet" title="German alphabet">German</a> alphabets, ⟨ee⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span> (though it is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> in majority of northern Dutch dialects). In <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>, ⟨ee⟩ is used for plain <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span>, as ⟨e⟩ stands for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɯ/</span></p>
<p>⟨<b>eh</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e̤/</span>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wade-Giles" title="Wade-Giles">Wade-Giles</a> transliteration of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> after a consonant, as in <i>yeh</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jɛ/</span>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_alphabet" title="German alphabet">German alphabet</a>, ⟨eh⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span>, as in <i>Reh</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>ei</b>⟩ usually represents a <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a>, ⟨ei⟩ can represent many sounds, including <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span>, as in <i>vein</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> as in <i>seize</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span> as in <i>heist</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> as in <i>heifer</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/æ/</span> as in <i>enceinte</i>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> as in <i>forfeit</i>. See also <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/I_before_e_except_after_c" title="I before e except after c">I before e except after c</a>. In the southern and western <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> dialects, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span>, while in the northern and eastern dialects, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔɪ/</span>.</p>
<p>In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_alphabet" title="Welsh alphabet">Welsh alphabet</a>, ⟨ei⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/əi/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_alphabet" title="Scottish Gaelic alphabet">Scottish Gaelic</a> orthographies, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> before a slender consonant. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_alphabet" title="Dutch alphabet">Dutch alphabet</a>, ⟨ei⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛi/</span>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_alphabet" title="German alphabet">German alphabet</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span>, as in <i>Einstein</i>. This digraph was taken over from <a href="/wiki/Middle_High_German" title="Middle High German">Middle High German</a> writing systems, where it represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span>. In Modern German, ⟨ei⟩ is predominant in representing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span>, while the equivalent digraph ⟨ai⟩ appears in only a few words. In <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a>, ⟨ei⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>, as in <i>seiche</i>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>eî</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛː/</span>, as in <i>reître</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁɛːtʁ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>éi</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span> between slender consonants.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ej</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_Language" title="Swedish Language">Swedish Language</a> in some short words. <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eːj/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>em</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐĩ̯ ~ ẽĩ̯/</span> at the end of a word and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ẽ/</span> before a consonant. In French orthography, it can represent /ɑ̃/.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ém</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐĩ̯ ~ ẽĩ̯/</span> at the end of a word.</p>
<p>⟨<b>êm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐĩ̯ ~ ẽĩ̯/</span> at the end of a word and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ẽ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>en</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐĩ̯ ~ ẽĩ̯/</span> at the end of a word followed or not by an <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> as in <i>hífen</i> or <i>hifens</i>; and for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ẽ/</span> before a consonant within a word. In <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑ̃/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>én</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɐĩ̯ ~ ẽĩ̯/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ên</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ẽ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>eo</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oː/</span> or occasionally <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant. In the <a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a> romanization of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canton_dialect" title="Canton dialect">Cantonese</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɵ/</span>, an allophone of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œː/</span>.
