In the <a href="/wiki/Revised_Romanization_of_Korean" title="Revised Romanization of Korean">Revised Romanization of Korean</a>, ⟨eo⟩ represents the <a href="/wiki/Open-mid_back_unrounded_vowel" title="Open-mid back unrounded vowel">open-mid back unrounded vowel</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʌ/</span>, and in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛu̯/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> ⟨eo⟩ is a rare digraph without a single pronunciation, representing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> in <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feoff" title="Feoff">feoff</a></i>, <i>jeopardy</i>, <i>leopard</i> and the given name <i>Geoffrey</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> in <i>people</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> in <i><a href="/wiki/Yeoman" title="Yeoman">yeoman</a></i> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/juː/</span> in the archaic <i><a href="/wiki/Vassal" title="Vassal">feodary</a></i>, while in the originally Gaelic name <a href="/wiki/MacLeod" title="MacLeod">MacLeod</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aʊ/</span>. However, usually it represents two vowels, like <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː.ə/</span> in <i>leotard</i> and <i>galleon</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː.oʊ/</span> in <i>stereo</i> and, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː.ɒ/</span> in <i><a href="/wiki/Geodesy" title="Geodesy">geodesy</a></i>, and, uniquely, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː.iː/</span> in <i><a href="/wiki/Geoduck" title="Geoduck">geoduck</a></i>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>eq</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">pharyngealized</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eˤ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>eu</b>⟩ is found in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>, most commonly for the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eu/</span>. Additionally, in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a>, ⟨eu⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/juː/</span> as in <i>neuter</i> (though in yod dropping accents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> may occur); however, the <i>eu</i> in "maneuver/manoeuvre" always represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> even in most yod retaining accents. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_alphabet" title="German alphabet">German alphabet</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔʏ/</span> as in <i>Deutsch</i>; and in the <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_alphabet" title="Dutch alphabet">Dutch</a>, <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> orthographies, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ø/</span> as in <i>feu</i>. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents either long <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/øː ~ œː/</span> and short <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œ/</span> or long <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eː/</span> and short <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-8"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-5"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Cantonese" title="Yale romanization of Cantonese">Yale romanization of Cantonese</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œː/</span>. In the orthographies of <a href="/wiki/Sundanese_language" title="Sundanese language">Sundanese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Acehnese_language" title="Acehnese language">Acehnese</a>, both <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian languages</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɤ/</span> as in <i>beureum</i> ('red'). In the <a href="/wiki/Revised_Romanization_of_Korean" title="Revised Romanization of Korean">Revised Romanization of Korean</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɯ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>eû</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ø/</span>, as in <i>jeûne</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒøn/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ew</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/juː/</span> as in <i>few</i> and <i>flew</i>. An exception is the pronunciation <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> in <i>sew</i>, leading to the <a href="/wiki/Heteronym_(linguistics)" title="Heteronym (linguistics)">heteronym</a> <i>sewer</i>,(<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈsuːər/</span>, 'drain') vs <i>sewer</i> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈsoʊər/</span>, 'one who sews'). In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it stands for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛʊ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-9"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-6"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-6"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>êw</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Kernowek_Standard" title="Kernowek Standard">Kernowek Standard</a> orthography of <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> to refer to a sound that can be either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛʊ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span>. This distribution can also be written ⟨ôw⟩.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-10"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ey</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for a variety of sounds, including <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> in <i>they</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> in <i>key</i>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span> in <i>geyser</i>. In the <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> alphabet, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛɪ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛɪ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/əɪ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-11"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-7"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-7"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-8"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="F">F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>ff</b>⟩ which may be written as the single unit: ﬀ, is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-9"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> for the same sound as single ⟨f⟩, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>. The doubling is used to indicate that the preceding vowel is (historically) short, or for <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymological</a> reasons, in <a href="/wiki/Latinism" title="Latinism">latinisms</a>. Very rarely, ⟨ff⟩ may be found word-initially in English, such as in proper names (e.g. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rose_ffrench" title="Rose ffrench">Rose ffrench</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jasper_Fforde" title="Jasper Fforde">Jasper Fforde</a>). In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_alphabet" title="Welsh alphabet">Welsh alphabet</a>, ⟨ff⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>, while ⟨f⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/v/</span>. In Welsh, ⟨ff⟩ is considered a distinct letter, and placed between ⟨f⟩ and ⟨g⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>. In medieval <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a>, vowel nasalisation was represented by a following ⟨ff⟩. This notation was reformed during the 18th century, though proper names retain the former convention, which leads to occasional mispronunciation. For ﬀ as a single unit see: <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">Typographic ligature</a> and Unicode FB00 (U+FB00) in <a href="/wiki/Latin_script_in_Unicode" title="Latin script in Unicode">Latin script in Unicode</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unicode_equivalence" title="Unicode equivalence">Unicode equivalence</a></p>
<p>⟨<b>fh</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">lenition</a> of ⟨f⟩. This happens to be silent, so that ⟨fh⟩ in Irish corresponds to no sound at all. For example, the phrase <span lang="ga" xml:lang="ga"><i>cá fhad</i></span> ('how long') is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Irish" title="Help:IPA for Irish">[kaː ad̪ˠ]</a></span>, where <span lang="ga" xml:lang="ga"><i>fhad</i></span> is the lenited form of <span lang="ga" xml:lang="ga"><i>fad</i></span> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/fɑd/</span> ('long').</p>
<p>⟨<b>fx</b>⟩ in used in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɸʔ/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="G">G</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: G">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>gʻ</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a> orthography to represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁ/</span> (Cyrillic ⟨ғ⟩). Technically it is not a digraph, since ⟨ʻ⟩ is not a letter of the Uzbek alphabet, but rather a typographic convention for a diacritic. In handwriting the letter is written ⟨ḡ⟩ or ⟨ğ⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gb</b>⟩ is used in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">African languages</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_labial-velar_plosive" title="Voiced labial-velar plosive">voiced labial-velar plosive</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ͡b/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gc</b>⟩ is used in alphabets for languages such as <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᶢǀ/</span> . In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a>, it indicates the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">eclipsis</a> of c and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ge</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span> before ⟨a o u⟩ as in <i>geôle</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒol/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gg</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> before ⟨i⟩ and ⟨e⟩. It is also used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>. In the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic orthography</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/çː/</span>. In the ISO romanization of <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, it is used for the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k͈/</span>, otherwise spelled ⟨kk⟩ (e.g. <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ggakdugi" title="Ggakdugi">ggakdugi</a></i>). In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kxʼ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, ⟨gg⟩ before a <a href="/wiki/Front_vowel" title="Front vowel">front vowel</a> represents a geminated <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>, as in <i>legge</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈled.dʒe/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lombard_language" title="Lombard language">Lombard</a>, ⟨gg⟩ is an etymological spelling representing an <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> at the end of a word which is the unvoicing of an ancient <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Gh_(digraph)" title="Gh (digraph)">gh</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages. In English, it can be silent or represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gi</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">Vietnamese alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span> in northern dialects and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> in the southern ones. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_alphabet" title="Italian alphabet">Italian alphabet</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span> before the non-front vowel letters ⟨a o u⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gj</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Albanian_alphabet" title="Albanian alphabet">Albanian alphabet</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_plosive" title="Voiced palatal plosive">voiced palatal plosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɟ/</span>, though for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gheg" title="Gheg">Gheg</a> speakers it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh_language" title="Arbëresh language">Arbëresh</a> dialect, it represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_plosive" title="Voiced velar plosive">voiced velar plosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡʲ/</span>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_alphabet" title="Norwegian alphabet">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_alphabet" title="Swedish alphabet">Swedish</a> alphabets, ⟨gj⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span> in words like <i>gjorde</i> ('did'). In <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>. It is also used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Macedonian" title="Romanization of Macedonian">Romanization of Macedonian</a> as a Latin equivalent of <a href="/wiki/Macedonian_alphabet" title="Macedonian alphabet">Cyrillic</a> ⟨<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D0%83" title="Ѓ">Ѓ</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gk</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_language" title="Sandawe language">Sandawe</a> and the romanization of <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span>; in <a href="/wiki/Limburgish_language" title="Limburgish language">Limburgish</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gl</b>⟩ is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_alphabet" title="Italian alphabet">Italian alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span> before ⟨i⟩. Elsewhere <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span> is represented by the trigraph ⟨gli⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span> in a few words of Greek origin, such as <i>phlegm</i> and <i>paradigm.</i> Between vowels, it simply represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡm/</span>, as in <i>paradigmatic.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>gn</b>⟩ is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_spelling_and_phonology" title="Latin spelling and phonology">Latin orthography</a>, where it represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋn/</span> in the classical period. Latin <a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">velar</a>-<a href="/wiki/Coronal_consonant" title="Coronal consonant">coronal</a> sequences like this (and also ⟨cl cr ct gd gl gr x⟩) underwent a <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(sound_change)" title="Palatalization (sound change)">palatal</a> mutation to varying degrees in most <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italo-Western" title="Italo-Western">Italo-Western</a> <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>. For most languages that preserve the ⟨gn⟩ spelling (such as <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>), it represents a <a href="/wiki/Palatal_nasal" title="Palatal nasal">palatal nasal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>. This was not the case in <a href="/wiki/Dalmatian_language" title="Dalmatian language">Dalmatian</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Romance_languages" title="Eastern Romance languages">Eastern Romance languages</a> where a different mutation changed the velar component to a <a href="/wiki/Labial_consonant" title="Labial consonant">labial consonant</a> as well as the spelling to ⟨mn⟩.</p>
<dl>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English orthography</a>, ⟨gn⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> initially (see <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#gn" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">/gn/ reduction</a>) and finally (i.e. <i>gnome, gnu, benign, sign</i>). When it appears between two syllables, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡn/</span> (e.g. <i>signal</i>). In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Norwegian_alphabet" title="Norwegian alphabet">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Swedish_alphabet" title="Swedish alphabet">Swedish</a> alphabets, ⟨gn⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋn/</span> in monosyllabic words like <i>agn</i>, and between two syllables, <i>tegne</i>. Initially, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡn/</span>, e.g. Swedish <i>gnista</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈɡnɪsta/</span>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>gñ</b>⟩ was used in several Spanish-derived orthographies of the Pacific for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>. It is one of several variants of the digraph ⟨ñg⟩, and is preserved in the name of the town of <a href="/wiki/Sag%C3%B1ay,_Camarines_Sur" title="Sagñay, Camarines Sur">Sagñay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>go</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> alphabet for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡw/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gq</b>⟩ is used in alphabets for languages such as <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᶢǃ/</span>. In the orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɢ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gr</b>⟩ is used in the orthography for <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣ̈/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gu</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_orthography" title="Catalan orthography">Catalan</a> orthographies for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> before front vowels ⟨i e⟩ (⟨i e y⟩ in English and French) where a "soft g" pronunciation (English <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>; Spanish <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>; French, Portuguese and Catalan <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span>) would otherwise occur. In English, it can also be used to represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡw/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet, it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gü</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">Spanish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_orthography" title="Catalan orthography">Catalan</a> orthographies for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡw/</span> before front vowels ⟨i e⟩ where the digraph ⟨gu⟩ would otherwise represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gv</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">Standard Zhuang</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> it is used for the supposed affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ͡bɣ͡β/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gw</b>⟩ is used in various languages for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡʷ/</span>, and in the orthography for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dene_Suline_language" title="Dene Suline language">Dene Suline</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ǥw</b>⟩, capital ⟨<b>Ǥw</b>⟩ (or ⟨<b>G̱w</b>⟩), is used in Alaskan <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_language" title="Tlingit language">Tlingit</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʷ/</span>; in Canada, this sound is represented by ⟨<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ghw_(trigraph)" title="Ghw (trigraph)">ghw</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gx</b>⟩ is used in alphabets for languages such as <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᶢǁ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Esperanto_orthography" title="Esperanto orthography">Esperanto orthography</a>, it is an unofficial variant of ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C4%9C" title="Ĝ">ĝ</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>gy</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_alphabet" title="Hungarian alphabet">Hungarian alphabet</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_plosive" title="Voiced palatal plosive">voiced palatal plosive</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɟ/</span>. In Hungarian, the letter's name is <i>gyé.</i> It is considered a single letter, and <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronyms</a> keep the digraph intact. The letter appears frequently in Hungarian words, such as the word for "Hungarian" itself: <i>magyar</i>. In the old orthography of <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>, it was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɕ/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="H">H</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: H">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>hh</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa language</a> to write the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_glottal_fricative" title="Voiced glottal fricative">murmured glottal fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɦ̤/</span>, though this is often written <i>h.</i> In the <a href="/wiki/Iraqw_language" title="Iraqw language">Iraqw language</a>, <i>hh</i> is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_epiglottal_fricative" title="Voiceless epiglottal fricative">voiceless epiglottal fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʜ/</span>, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dene_Suline_language" title="Dene Suline language">Chipewyan</a> it is a velar/uvular <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/χ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">Esperanto</a>, it is an official surrogate of <i><a href="/wiki/%C4%A4" title="Ĥ">ĥ</a></i>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>hj</b>⟩ is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arb%C3%ABresh_language" title="Arbëresh language">Italian dialect of Albanian</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʲ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, it represents either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> it is used to denote <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ç/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>hl</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɬ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l̥/</span> in various alphabets, such as the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɬ/</span>) and <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l̥/</span>). See also <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#HL" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">reduction of Old English /hl/</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>hm</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m̥/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>hn</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n̥/</span>. It is also used in <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> to denote the same phoneme. See also <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#HL" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">reduction of Old English /hn/</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>hr</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r̥/</span>. See also <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#HL" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">reduction of Old English /hr/</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>hs</b>⟩ is used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wade-Giles" title="Wade-Giles">Wade-Giles</a> transcription of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a> for the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɕ/</span>, equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> <i>x.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>hu</b>⟩ is used primarily in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Nahuatl" title="Classical Nahuatl">Classical Nahuatl</a> language, in which it represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> sound before a vowel; for example, <i>Wikipedia</i> in Nahuatl is written <i>Huiquipedia</i>. After a vowel, ⟨uh⟩ is used. In the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet, <i>hu</i> was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁʷ/</span>, similar to French <i>roi.</i> The sequence <i>hu</i> is also found in Spanish words such as <i>huevo</i> or <i>hueso;</i> however, in Spanish this is not a digraph but a simple sequence of silent <i>h</i> and the vowel <i>u.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>hv</b>⟩ is used <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Icelandic_language" title="Icelandic language">Icelandic</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kv/</span> (often <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kf/</span>), generally in <a href="/wiki/Interrogative_word" title="Interrogative word">wh-words</a>, but also in other words, such as Faroese <i>hvonn</i>. In the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> it is used for the supposed fricative <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣ͜β/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><span id="hw">hw</span></b>⟩ was used in <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hw/</span>. It is now spelled ⟨<a href="#wh">wh</a>⟩ (see there for more details). It is used in some orthographies of <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʍ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-8"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-10"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>hx</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a> (⟨h⟩ alone represents the fricative <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>), and in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> it is a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hʔ/</span>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-convention" title="X-convention">Esperanto</a> it is an unofficial surrogate of ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C4%A4" title="Ĥ">ĥ</a>⟩.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="I">I</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: I">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>i′</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> or <a href="/wiki/Creaky_voice" title="Creaky voice">creaky</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ḭ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ie</b>⟩ is found in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, where it usually represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪ/</span> sound as in <i>pries</i> and <i>allied</i> or the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> sound as in <i>priest</i> and <i>rallied</i>. Followed by an <i>r</i>, these vowels follow the standard changes to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪə/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪə/</span>, as in <i>brier</i> and <i>bier</i>. Unique pronunciations are <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/</span> in <i>sieve</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> in <i>friend</i> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> in <i>lingerie</i>. Unstressed it can represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jə/</span>, as in <i>spaniel</i> and <i>conscience</i>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> as in <i>mischief</i> and <i>hurriedly</i>. It also can represent many vowel combinations, including <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪə/</span> in <i>diet</i> and <i>client</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aɪɛ/</span> in <i>diester</i> and <i>quiescent</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iːə/</span> in <i>alien</i> and <i>skier</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iːɛ/</span> in <i>oriental</i> and <i>hygienic</i>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iːʔiː/</span> in British <i>medieval</i>.</p>
<dl>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, the ⟨<b>ie</b>⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, it may represent the lengthened vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> as in <i>L<b>ie</b>be</i> (love) as well as the vowel combination <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iə/</span> as in <i>Belg<b>ie</b>n</i> (Belgium). In <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lithuanian_language" title="Lithuanian language">Lithuanian</a>, the ⟨<b>ie</b>⟩ is considered two letters for all purposes and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iæ̯/</span>, commonly (although less precisely) transcribed as <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i̯e/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Maltese_language" title="Maltese language">Maltese</a>, ⟨<b>ie</b>⟩ is a distinct letter and represents a long <a href="/wiki/Close_front_unrounded_vowel" title="Close front unrounded vowel">close front unrounded vowel</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span>) or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iɛ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> it is used to write the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>, where <i>e</i> stands for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>ig</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ʃ/</span> in the coda.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ih</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the breathy or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i̤/</span>. It is also used in <a href="/wiki/Tongyong_Pinyin" title="Tongyong Pinyin">Tongyong Pinyin</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wade-Giles" title="Wade-Giles">Wade-Giles</a> transcription for the fricative vowels of Mandarin Chinese, which are spelled <i>i</i> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ii</b>⟩ is used in many languages with phonemic long vowels for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/IJ_(digraph)" title="IJ (digraph)">ij</a></b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_orthography" title="Dutch orthography">Dutch</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛi/</span>. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>il</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/j/</span>, historically <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span>, as in <i>ail</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aj/</span> "garlic".</p>
<p>⟨<b>im</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ĩ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ím</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ĩ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>in</b>⟩ is used in many languages to write a <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">nasal vowel</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> before a consonant, and in many <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> languages, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ĩ/</span>, while in French it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ín</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ĩ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>în</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write a vowel sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span> that was once followed by a historical <i>s</i>, as in <i>vous vîntes</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/vu vɛ̃t/</span> "you came".</p>
<p>⟨<b>iŋ</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lakhota_language" title="Lakhota language">Lakhota</a> for the nasal vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ĩ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>io</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʊ/</span>, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ío</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>iq</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, it represents the <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">pharyngealized</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iˤ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>iu</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʊ/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant. In Mandarin <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i̯ou̯/</span> after a consonant. (In initial position, this is spelled <i>you.</i>)</p>
<p>⟨<b>iú</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> between a slender and a broad consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>iw</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iʊ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪʊ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-8"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-9"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-11"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ix</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> after a vowel.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="J">J</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: J">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>jh</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Walloon_language" title="Walloon language">Walloon</a> to write a sound that is variously <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span>, depending on the dialect. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tongyong_pinyin" title="Tongyong pinyin">Tongyong pinyin</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʂ/</span>, written <i>zh</i> in standard pinyin. <i>Jh</i> is also the standard transliteration for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Devan%C4%81gar%C4%AB" title="Devanāgarī">Devanāgarī</a> letter <b>झ</b> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒʱ/</span>. In the official <a href="/wiki/Esperanto_orthography" title="Esperanto orthography">Esperanto orthography</a>, it is a surrogate of <i><a href="/wiki/%C4%B4" title="Ĵ">ĵ</a></i>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>jj</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʑ/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>. In romanized <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, it represents the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɕ͈/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃʼ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>jö</b>⟩ is used as a letter of the <a href="/wiki/Seri_language" title="Seri language">Seri</a> alphabet, where it represents a <a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">labialized</a> <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">velar fricative</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʷ/</span>. It is placed between <a href="/wiki/J" title="J">J</a> and <a href="/wiki/L" title="L">L</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>jr</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɖʐ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>jx</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-convention" title="X-convention">Esperanto</a> as an unofficial surrogate of ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C4%B4" title="Ĵ">ĵ</a>⟩.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="K">K</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: K">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>kf</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the supposed affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k͡px͡ɸ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kg</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kχ/</span> in southern African languages such as <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Setswana</a>. For instance, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kalahari" title="Kalahari">Kalahari</a> is spelled <i>Kgalagadi</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kχalaχadi/</span> in Setswana.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kh</b>⟩, in transcriptions of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_language" title="Indo-Aryan language">Indo-Aryan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dravidian_languages" title="Dravidian languages">Dravidian languages</a>, represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">aspirated</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_plosive" title="Voiceless velar plosive">voiceless velar plosive</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʰ/</span>). For scores of other languages, it represents the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_velar_fricative" title="Voiceless velar fricative">voiceless velar fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x/</span>, for example in transcriptions of the letter <i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Semitic transliteration"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%E1%B8%A4%C4%81%CA%BC" title="Ḥāʼ">ḥāʼ</a></span></i> (<span lang="ar" xml:lang="ar">خ</span>) in standard Arabic, standard Persian, and Urdu, Cyrillic <i>Х</i>, <i>х</i> (kha), Spanish <i>j</i>, etc. As the transcription of the letter <i><span class="Unicode" style="white-space:normal; text-decoration: none" title="Semitic transliteration"><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%E1%B8%A4et" title="Ḥet">ḥet</a></span></i> (<span class="script-hebrew" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 115%; font-family: Alef, 'SBL BibLit', 'SBL Hebrew', 'David CLM', 'Frenk Ruehl CLM', 'Hadasim CLM', Cardo, Shofar, David, 'Ezra SIL', 'Ezra SIL SR', 'Noto Sans Hebrew', FreeSerif, 'Times New Roman', FreeSans, Arial;">ח</span>‎) in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sephardic_Hebrew" title="Sephardic Hebrew">Sephardic Hebrew</a>, it represents the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_pharyngeal_fricative" title="Voiceless pharyngeal fricative">voiceless pharyngeal fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ħ/</span>. It is also used to transcribe the Hebrew letter <a href="/wiki/Kaph" title="Kaph">kaf</a> (<span class="script-hebrew" dir="rtl" style="font-size: 115%; font-family: Alef, 'SBL BibLit', 'SBL Hebrew', 'David CLM', 'Frenk Ruehl CLM', 'Hadasim CLM', Cardo, Shofar, David, 'Ezra SIL', 'Ezra SIL SR', 'Noto Sans Hebrew', FreeSerif, 'Times New Roman', FreeSans, Arial;">כ</span>‎) in instances when the letter is <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">lenited</a>. When transliterating Russian, Ukrainian and Belorussian, all written only in the Cyrillic alphabet, the digraph is equivalent to the Cyrillic letter <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%D0%A5" title="Х">Х</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dd>In Canadian <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_language" title="Tlingit language">Tlingit</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʰ/</span>, which in Alaska is written <i><u>k</u>.</i> In the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet, it was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʼ/</span>.</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>kj</b>⟩ is used <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɕ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ç/</span>. See also ⟨tj⟩. In <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kk</b>⟩ is used in Icelandic and Faroese for the pre-aspirated sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʰk/</span>, in romanized <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a> for the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k͈/</span>, and in Haida (Bringhurst orthography) for ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʼ/</span>,in Finnish for a geminate constant <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kː/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kl</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu language</a> to write a sound variously realized as <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʟ̥ʼ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kxʼ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>km</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nasal_release" title="Nasal release">nasally released</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k͡pŋ͡m/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kn</b>⟩ is used in English to write the word-initial sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> (<a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#kn" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">formerly pronounced /kn/</a>) in some words of Germanic origin, such as <i>knee</i> and <i>knife.</i> It is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Nasal_release" title="Nasal release">nasally released</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kŋ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kp</b>⟩ is used as a letter in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">African languages</a>, where it represents a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_labial-velar_plosive" title="Voiceless labial-velar plosive">voiceless labial-velar plosive</a> (simultaneous <i>k</i> and <i>p</i>: <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k͡p/</span>).</p>
<p>⟨<b>kr</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa language</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kxʼ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ks</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish language</a> for either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ks/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡz/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-10"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-12"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ku</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pur%C3%A9pecha_language" title="Purépecha language">Purépecha</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span>. It also had that value in the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kv</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷʰ/</span> in some dialects of <a href="/wiki/Zhuang_languages" title="Zhuang languages">Zhuang</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><span id="kw">kw</span></b>⟩ is used in various languages for the <a href="/wiki/Labialized_velar_consonant" title="Labialized velar consonant">labialized velar consonant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span>, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dene_Suline_language" title="Dene Suline language">Dene Suline</a> (Chipewyan) for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷʰ/</span>. Used informally in English for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phonemic_spelling" title="Phonemic spelling">phonemic spelling</a> of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Qu_(digraph)" title="Qu (digraph)">qu</a></i>, as in <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/kwik" title="wikt:kwik">kwik</a></i> (from <i>quick</i>), ultimately from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">*/kʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ḵw</b>⟩ is used in Alaskan <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_language" title="Tlingit language">Tlingit</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʷʰ/</span>, which in Canada is written <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Khw_(trigraph)" title="Khw (trigraph)">khw</a>.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>kx</b>⟩ in used in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʔ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ky</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetan_Pinyin" title="Tibetan Pinyin">Tibetan Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃʰ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>kz</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡz/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Esperanto" title="Esperanto">Esperanto</a>, though some speakers pronounce it <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kz/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="L">L</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: L">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>lh</b>⟩, in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Occitan" title="Occitan">Occitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gallo_language" title="Gallo language">Gallo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, represents a <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">palatal lateral approximant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span>. In many <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_languages_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous languages of the Americas">Indigenous languages of the Americas</a> it represents a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_lateral_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolar lateral fricative">voiceless alveolar lateral fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɬ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> it represents a dental lateral, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l̪/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Gwoyeu_Romatzyh" title="Gwoyeu Romatzyh">Gwoyeu Romatzyh</a> romanization of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, initial ⟨lh⟩ indicates an even tone on a syllable beginning in <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l/</span>, which is otherwise spelled ⟨l⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>lj</b>⟩ is a letter in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_language" title="Slavic language">Slavic languages</a>, such as the Latin orthographies of <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">Serbo-Croatian</a>, where it represents a <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">palatal lateral approximant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span>. For example, the word <i>ljiljan</i> is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎiʎan/</span>. <a href="/wiki/Ljudevit_Gaj" title="Ljudevit Gaj">Ljudevit Gaj</a> first used the digraph ⟨lj⟩ in 1830; he devised it by analogy with a <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic</a> digraph, which developed into the <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">ligature</a> <a href="/wiki/Lje" title="Lje">љ</a>.</p>
<dl>
<dd>The sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span> is written ⟨gl⟩ in Italian, in Castilian Spanish and Catalan as ⟨ll⟩, in Portuguese as ⟨lh⟩, in some Hungarian dialects as ⟨lly⟩, and in <a href="/wiki/Latvian_language" title="Latvian language">Latvian</a> as ⟨ļ⟩. In <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a> and <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">Slovak</a>, it is often transcribed as ⟨ľ⟩; it is used more frequently in the latter language. There are dedicated Unicode glyphs, ǉ, ǈ, and Ǉ.</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Ll" title="Ll">ll</a></b>⟩ and ⟨<b><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/L%C2%B7l" title="L·l">l·l</a></b>⟩ are used in several languages. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ḷḷ</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Asturian_language" title="Asturian language">Asturian</a> for a sound that was historically <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʎ/</span> but which is now an affricate, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡s], [t͡ʃ], [d͡ʒ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>lr</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɭ /</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>lv</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/l͜β/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>lw</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/lʷ/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>lx</b>⟩ in used in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀl/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Hungarian_ly" title="Hungarian ly">ly</a></b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>. See article.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="M">M</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: M">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>mb</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mb/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐb/</span>. It is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> to indicate the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">eclipsis</a> of <i>b</i> and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mˠ/</span>; for example <i>ár mbád</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑːɾˠ mˠɑːdˠ̪/</span> "our boat" (cf. <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bˠɑːd̪ˠ/</span> "boat"). The Irish digraph is capitalized <b>mB</b>, for example <i>i <b>mB</b>aile Átha Cliath</i> "in Dublin". In English, <i>mb</i> represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span> when final, as in <i>lamb</i> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/-mb" title="-mb">reduction of /mb/</a>). In <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">Standard Zhuang</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>, ⟨<b>mb</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɓ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>md</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prenasalized" title="Prenasalized">prenasalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n͡mt͡p/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mf</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mf/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐf/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mg</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋɡ/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>, where the more common diacritic ⟨ng⟩ is restricted to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>. It is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prenasalized" title="Prenasalized">prenasalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ͡mk͡p/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mh</b>⟩, in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, stands for the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">lenition</a> of ⟨<b>m</b>⟩ and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/v/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span>; for example <i>mo mháthair</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mə ˈwɑːhəɾʲ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mˠə ˈvˠɑːhəɾʲ/</span> "my mother" (cf. <i>máthair</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈmˠɑːhəɾʲ/</span> "mother"). In <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a> it stands for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_morphology" title="Welsh morphology">nasal mutation</a> of ⟨<b>p</b>⟩ and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m̥/</span>; for example <i>fy mhen</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/və m̥ɛn/</span> "my head" (cf. <i>pen</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pɛn/</span> "head"). In both languages it is considered a sequence of the two letters ⟨<b>m</b>⟩ and ⟨<b>h</b>⟩ for purposes of alphabetization. It also occurs in <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Gwoyeu_Romatzyh" title="Gwoyeu Romatzyh">Gwoyeu Romatzyh</a> romanization of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, initial <i>mh-</i> indicates an even tone on a syllable beginning in <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span>, which is otherwise spelled <i>m-.</i> In several languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Gogo_language" title="Gogo language">Gogo</a>, it's a voiceless <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m̥/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ml</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mˡ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mm</b>⟩ is used in Haida (Bringhurst orthography) for glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀm/</span>. It is used in <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for an optionally <a href="/wiki/Pre-stopped_consonant" title="Pre-stopped consonant">pre-occluded</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span>; that is, it is pronounced either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mː/</span> (in any position); <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵇm/</span> (before a consonant or finally); or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/bm/</span> (before a vowel); examples are <i>mamm</i> ('mother') or <i>hemma</i> ('this').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-9"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-11"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-13"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>mn</b>⟩ is used in English to write the word-initial sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> in a few words of Greek origin, such as <i>mnemonic.</i> When final, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m/</span>, as in <i>damn</i>, and between vowels it represents /m/ as in <i>damning</i>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mn/</span> as in <i>damnation</i> (see <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#mb" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">/mn/-reduction</a>). In <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>, as in <i>automne</i> and <i>condamner.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>mp</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mp/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐp/</span>. Modern Greek uses the equivalent digraph <a href="/wiki/Mu_(letter)" title="Mu (letter)">μ</a><a href="/wiki/Pi_(letter)" title="Pi (letter)">π</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/b/</span>, as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beta_(letter)" title="Beta (letter)">β</a> is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/v/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Mpumpong_language" title="Mpumpong language">Mpumpong</a> of <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, ⟨mp⟩ is a plain <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mt</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prenasalized" title="Prenasalized">prenasalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n̪͡mt̪͡p/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mv</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mv/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐv/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mw</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mʷ/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>mx</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀm/</span>.</p>
