<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>n’</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>. Since ⟨’⟩ is not a letter in either language, ⟨n’⟩ is not technically a digraph.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nb</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mb/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nc</b>⟩ is used in various alphabets. In the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲɟ/</span>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tharaka_language" title="Tharaka language">Tharaka</a> it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ntʃ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> it represents the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǀ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nd</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nd/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿd/</span>, and capitalized ⟨<b>Nd</b>⟩. It is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">eclipsis</a> of ⟨d⟩, and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>, for example in <i>ár ndoras</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑːɾˠ ˈnˠɔɾˠəsˠ/</span> "our door" (cf. <i>doras</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈd̪ˠɔɾˠəsˠ/</span> "door"). In this function it is capitalized ⟨<b>nD</b>⟩, e.g. <i>i <b>nD</b>oire</i> "in Derry". In <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">Standard Zhuang</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>, ⟨<b>nd</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɗ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nf</b>⟩, equivalent to ⟨<b>mf</b>⟩ for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mf/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐf/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Rangi_language" title="Rangi language">Rangi</a> <i>nf</i> is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐf/</span> while <i>mf</i> is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/m.f/</span>.</p>
<p><span id="ng"></span>⟨<b>ng</b>⟩, in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and several other <a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">European</a> and derived orthographies (for example <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>), generally represents the <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">velar nasal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>. It is considered a single letter in many <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_languages" title="Austronesian languages">Austronesian languages</a> (<a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">Māori</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tongan_language" title="Tongan language">Tongan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gilbertese_language" title="Gilbertese language">Kiribatian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuvaluan_language" title="Tuvaluan language">Tuvaluan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_language" title="Indonesian language">Indonesian</a>), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Welsh_Language" title="Welsh Language">Welsh</a> language, and <a href="/wiki/Rheinische_Dokumenta" title="Rheinische Dokumenta">Rheinische Dokumenta</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">velar nasal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>; and in some <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/African_languages" title="African languages">African languages</a> (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lingala_language" title="Lingala language">Lingala</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bambara_language" title="Bambara language">Bambara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wolof_language" title="Wolof language">Wolof</a>) for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prenasalization" title="Prenasalization">prenasalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/<a href="/wiki/Voiced_velar_stop" title="Voiced velar stop">ɡ</a>/</span> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿɡ/</span>).</p>
<dl>
<dd>For the development of the pronunciation of this digraph in English, see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NG-coalescence" title="NG-coalescence">NG-coalescence</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-dropping" title="G-dropping">G-dropping</a>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>The <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish language</a> uses the digraph 'ng' to denote the phonemically long <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">velar nasal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋː/</span> in contrast to 'nk' <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋk/</span>, which is its "strong" form under <a href="/wiki/Consonant_gradation" title="Consonant gradation">consonant gradation</a>, a type of <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">lenition</a>. Weakening <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> produces an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Archiphoneme" title="Archiphoneme">archiphonemic</a> "velar fricative", which, as a velar fricative does not exist in Standard Finnish, is assimilated to the preceding <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>, producing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋː/</span>. (No <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> is involved at any point, despite the spelling 'ng'.) The digraph 'ng' is not an independent letter, but it is an exception to the <a href="/wiki/Phonemic_orthography" title="Phonemic orthography">phonemic principle</a>, one of the few in standard Finnish.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> <i>ng</i> is used word-initially as the <a href="/wiki/Irish_initial_mutations" title="Irish initial mutations">eclipsis</a> of <i>g</i> and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>, e.g. <i>ár ngalar</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɑːɾˠ ˈŋɑɫəɾˠ/</span> "our illness" (cf. <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈɡɑɫəɾˠ/</span>). In this function it is capitalized <i>nG</i>, e.g. <i>i</i> nG<i>aillimh</i> "in Galway".</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>In Tagalog and other <a href="/wiki/Philippine_languages" title="Philippine languages">Philippine languages</a>, <i>ng</i> represented the prenasalized sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋɡ/</span> during the Spanish era. The velar nasal, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>, was written in a variety of ways, namely "n͠g", "ñg", "gñ" (as in <a href="/wiki/Sag%C3%B1ay,_Camarines_Sur" title="Sagñay, Camarines Sur">Sagñay</a>), and—after a vowel—at times "g̃". During the standardization of Tagalog in the early part of the 20th century, <i>ng</i> became used for the velar nasal <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>, while prenasalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋɡ/</span> came to be written <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ngg_(trigraph)" title="Ngg (trigraph)">ngg</a>.</i> Furthermore, <i>ng</i> is also used for a common <a href="/wiki/Genitive_case" title="Genitive case">genitive</a> particle pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/naŋ/</span>, to differentiate it from an adverbial particle <i>nang.</i></dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>ńg</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a> to write the voiceless nasal sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ̊/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ñg</b>⟩, or more precisely ⟨<b>n͠g</b>⟩, was a digraph in several Spanish-derived orthographies of the Pacific, such as that of <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chamorro_language" title="Chamorro language">Chamorro</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> where it represented the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>, as opposed to <i>ng</i>, which originally represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋɡ/</span>. An example is Chamorro <i>agan͠gñáijon</i> (modern <i>agangñaihon)</i> "to declare". Besides <i>ñg</i>, variants of <i>n͠g</i> include <i>gñ</i> (as in <a href="/wiki/Sag%C3%B1ay,_Camarines_Sur" title="Sagñay, Camarines Sur">Sagñay</a>), <i>ng̃</i>, and a <i>g̃</i>, that is preceded by a vowel (but not a consonant). It has since been replaced by the trigraph ⟨<b>ngg</b>⟩ or ⟨<b>ng</b>⟩ (see above).</p>
<p>⟨<b>ng’</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span> in Swahili and languages with Swahili-based orthographies. Since ⟨’⟩ is not a letter in Swahili, ⟨ng’⟩ is technically a digraph, not a <a href="/wiki/Trigraph_(orthography)" title="Trigraph (orthography)">trigraph</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Nh_(digraph)" title="Nh (digraph)">nh</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ni</b>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Polish_orthography" title="Polish orthography">Polish orthography</a>, it usually represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɲ</span> whenever it precedes a vowel, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɲi</span> whenever it precedes a consonant (or in the end of the word), and is considered a graphic variant of <a href="/wiki/%C5%83" title="Ń">ń</a> appearing in other situations. (In some cases it may represent also <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">ɲj</span> before a vowel; for a better description, when, see <a href="/wiki/Polish_orthography#Other_issues_with_i_and_j" title="Polish orthography">the relevant section in the article on Polish orthography</a>).</p>
<p>⟨<b>nj</b>⟩ is a letter present in the Latin orthographies of <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbo-Croatian" title="Serbo-Croatian">Serbo-Croatian</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ljudevit_Gaj" title="Ljudevit Gaj">Ljudevit Gaj</a>, a Croat, first used this digraph in 1830. In all of these languages, it represents the <a href="/wiki/Palatal_nasal" title="Palatal nasal">palatal nasal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>. For example, the Croatian and Serbian word <i>konj</i> (<i>horse</i>) is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/koɲ/</span>. The digraph was created in the 19th century by analogy with a digraph of <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">Cyrillic</a>, which developed into the <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">ligature</a> ⟨<a href="/wiki/Nje" title="Nje">Њ</a>⟩. There are dedicated glyphs in Unicode, Ǌ, ǋ, ǌ.</p>
<dl>
<dd>In <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, it generally represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>, although in some words it represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nj/</span>, like in <i>banjo</i>. It is also used in some languages of <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Africa" title="Languages of Africa">Africa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Oceania" title="Languages of Oceania">Oceania</a> where it represents a <a href="/wiki/Prenasalized_consonant" title="Prenasalized consonant">prenazalized</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_affricate" title="Voiced postalveolar affricate">voiced postalveolar affricate</a> or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">fricative</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿdʒ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿʒ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿdz/</span>.</dd>
</dl>
<dl>
<dd>Other letters and digraphs of the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a> used for spelling this sound are ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%83" title="Ń">ń</a>⟩ (in <a href="/wiki/Polish_language" title="Polish language">Polish</a>), ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%87" title="Ň">ň</a>⟩ (in <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovakian_language" title="Slovakian language">Slovakian</a>), ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C3%91" title="Ñ">ñ</a>⟩ (in <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>), ⟨nh⟩ (in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>), ⟨gn⟩ (in <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a> and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>), and ⟨ny⟩ (in <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">Hungarian</a>, among others).</dd>
</dl>
<p>⟨<b>nk</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of many <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu languages</a> like <a href="/wiki/Lingala" title="Lingala">Lingala</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tshiluba" title="Tshiluba">Tshiluba</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kikongo" title="Kikongo">Kikongo</a>, for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋk/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑk/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a>, it distinguishes a prenasalized velar stop, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ͡k ~ ŋ͡ɡ/</span>, from the nasal <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nm</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n͡m/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ńm</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n̪͡m/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nn</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish orthography</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_Irish_language" title="Old Irish language">Old Irish</a> "<a href="/wiki/Irish_phonology#Fortis_and_lenis_sonorants" title="Irish phonology">fortis sonorants</a>" <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/Nˠ/</span> ("broad", i.e. non-palatalized or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Velarized" title="Velarized">velarized</a>) and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/Nʲ/</span> ("slender", i.e. <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(phonetics)" title="Palatalization (phonetics)">palatalized</a>) in non-initial position. In modern <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>, the "broad" sound is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n̪ˠ/</span>, while the slender sound can be any of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʲ/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n̠ʲ/</span>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>, depending on dialect and position in the word. In <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> historical ⟨<b>nn</b>⟩ has contracted to the <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">ligature</a> ⟨<b><a href="/wiki/%C3%91" title="Ñ">ñ</a></b>⟩ and represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Gwoyeu_Romatzyh" title="Gwoyeu Romatzyh">Gwoyeu Romatzyh</a> romanization of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, final <i>-nn</i> indicates a falling tone on a syllable ending in <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>, which is otherwise spelled <i>-n.</i> It is used in Haida (Bringhurst orthography) for glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀn/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a>, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋn/</span> in the middle of a word, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> at the end. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it is used for an optionally <a href="/wiki/Pre-stopped_consonant" title="Pre-stopped consonant">pre-occluded</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span>; that is, it is pronounced either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nː/</span> (in any position); <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵈn/</span> (before a consonant or finally); or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dn/</span> (before a vowel); examples are <i>penn</i> ('head') or <i>pennow</i> ('heads').<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-10"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-12"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-14"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>np</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mb/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nq</b>⟩ is used in various alphabets. In the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɴɢ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> it represents the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǃ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Gwoyeu_Romatzyh" title="Gwoyeu Romatzyh">Gwoyeu Romatzyh</a> romanization of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, final <i>-nq</i> indicates a falling tone on a syllable ending in <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span>, which is otherwise spelled <i>-ng.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>nr</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɳɖ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɳ /</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ns</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ns/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿs/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nt</b>⟩ is a letter present in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a> where it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nt/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿt/</span> .</p>
<p>⟨<b>nv</b>⟩, equivalent to ⟨<b>mv</b>⟩ for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mv/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵐv/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nw</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Igbo_language" title="Igbo language">Igbo</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋʷ/</span>, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nx</b>⟩ is used for the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǁ/</span> in alphabets such as <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀn/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Ny_(digraph)" title="Ny (digraph)">ny</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɲ/</span>. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>nz</b>⟩, in many <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">African</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Languages" title="Languages">languages</a>, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nz/</span> ~ <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿz/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ndz/</span> ~ <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿdz/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/nʒ/</span> ~ <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿʒ/</span>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ndʒ/</span> ~ <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⁿdʒ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>n-</b>⟩ is used for medial <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>o′</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> or <a href="/wiki/Creaky_voice" title="Creaky voice">creaky</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o̰/</span>. It is also used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ø/</span> in Romanized <a href="/wiki/Uzbek_language" title="Uzbek language">Uzbek</a>, with the preferred typographical form being ⟨<b>oʻ</b>⟩ (Cyrillic ⟨ў⟩). Technically it is not a digraph in Uzbek, since ⟨ʻ⟩ is not a letter of the Uzbek alphabet, but rather a typographic convention for a diacritic. In handwriting the letter is written ⟨ō⟩ or ⟨ŏ⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oa</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, where it commonly represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> sound as in <i>road</i>, <i>coal</i>, <i>boast</i>, <i>coaxing</i>, etc. In <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a>, where the digraph originated, it represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔː/</span>, a pronunciation retained in the word <i>broad</i> and derivatives, and when the digraph is followed by an "r", as in <i>soar</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Bezoar" title="Bezoar">bezoar</a></i>. The letters also represent two vowels, as in <i>koala</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ.ɑː/</span>, <i><a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Boa_(disambiguation)" title="Boa (disambiguation)">boas</a></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ.ə/</span>, <i><a href="/wiki/Coaxial" title="Coaxial">coaxial</a></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ.æ/</span>, <i>oasis</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ.eɪ/</span>, and <i>doable</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː.ə/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a>, it is occasionally used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oe</b>⟩ is found in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, it represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> sound as in <i>hoe</i> and sometimes the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> sound as in <i>shoe</i>. It may also represent the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/</span> sound in <a href="/wiki/American_English" title="American English">AmE</a> pronunciation of <i><a href="/wiki/Oedipus" title="Oedipus">Oedipus</a></i>, <i>(o)esophagus</i> (also in <a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">BrE</a>), and <i>(o)estrogen</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/eɪ/</span> in <i>boehmite</i> (AmE) and surnames like <i><a href="/wiki/John_Boehner" title="John Boehner">Boehner</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Matt_Groening" title="Matt Groening">Groening</a></i> (as if spelled <i>Bayner</i> and <i>Gray/Greyning</i> respectively), and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> in <i>foetus</i> (BrE and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_English" title="Commonwealth English">CoE</a>) and some speakers' pronunciation of <i>Oedipus</i> and <i>oestrogen</i>. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" title="Afrikaans language">Afrikaans</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> <i>oe</i> is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span>, as in <i>doen</i>. Often <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ligature_(typography)" title="Ligature (typography)">ligatured</a> to ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%92" title="Œ">œ</a>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a>, it stands for the vowels <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œ/</span> (as in <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">œil</span></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œj/</span>) and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/e/</span> (as in <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr">œsophage</span></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ezɔfaʒ ~ øzɔfaʒ/</span>). It is an alternative way to write ⟨ö⟩ in German when this character is unavailable. In <a href="/wiki/Cantonese_Pinyin" title="Cantonese Pinyin">Cantonese Pinyin</a> it represents the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɵ ~ œː/</span>, and in <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">Zhuang</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> (⟨o⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oː/</span>). In <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a>, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wɛ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Kernewek_Kemmyn" title="Kernewek Kemmyn">Kernewek Kemmyn</a> orthography of <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it is used for a phoneme which is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[oː]</span> long, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[oˑ]</span> mid-length, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ɤ]</span> short.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GerlyverMeur_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-GerlyverMeur-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>oê</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write the vowel sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wa/</span> in a few words before what had historically been an <i>s</i>, mostly in words derived from <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/po%C3%AAle" title="wikt:poêle">poêle</a></span></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pwal/</span> "stove". The diacriticless variant, ⟨oe⟩, rarely represents this sound except in words related to <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/moelle" title="wikt:moelle">moelle</a></span></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/mwal/</span> (rarely spelt <i><span lang="fr" xml:lang="fr"><a class="extiw" href="https://fr.wikipedia.org/wiki/wikt:mo%C3%ABlle" title="fr:wikt:moëlle">moëlle</a></span></i>).</p>
<p>⟨<b>õe</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/õĩ̯/</span>. It is used in plural forms of some words ended in ⟨ão⟩, such as <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/an%C3%A3o" title="wiktionary:anão">anão</a>–an<b>õe</b>s</i> and <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/campe%C3%A3o" title="wiktionary:campeão">campeão</a>–campe<b>õe</b>s.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>oh</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the breathy or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o̤/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oi</b>⟩ is used in various <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <i>oi</i> represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oɪ̯/</span> sound as in <i>coin</i> and <i>join</i>. In <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wa/</span>, which was historically – and still is in some cases – written "oy." In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ/, /ɔ/, /ɪ/, /əi̯/, /iː/, /oː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant. In <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a>, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ui̯/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oí</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oî</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wa/</span> before what had historically been an <i>s</i>, as in <i>boîtier</i> or <i>cloître.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>ói</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>òi</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oi̯/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>om</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/õ/</span>, and in French to write <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ̃/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ôm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/õ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>on</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/õ/</span> before a consonant, and in French to write <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ̃/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ôn</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/õ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ön</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetan_Pinyin" title="Tibetan Pinyin">Tibetan Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ø̃/</span>. It is alternately written <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oin_(trigraph)" title="Oin (trigraph)">oin</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oo</b>⟩ is used in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, <i>oo</i> commonly represents two sounds: <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> as in "m<i>oo</i>n" and "f<i>oo</i>d", and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʊ/</span> as in "w<i>oo</i>d" and "f<i>oo</i>t". Historically, both derive from the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oː/</span>, which is also the digraph’s pronunciation in most other languages. In <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, the digraph represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oː/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oː/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-12"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-11"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-13"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-15"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>oq</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">pharyngealized</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oˤ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>or</b>⟩, in <a href="/wiki/Daighi_tongiong_pingim" title="Daighi tongiong pingim">Daighi tongiong pingim</a>, represents <a href="/wiki/Mid_central_vowel" title="Mid central vowel">mid central vowel</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ə/</span> or <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">close-mid back rounded vowel</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Taiwanese_Hokkien" title="Taiwanese Hokkien">Taiwanese Hokkien</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ou</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aʊ/</span>, as in <i>out</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aʊt/</span>. This spelling is generally used before consonants, with ⟨ow⟩ being used instead before vowels and at the ends of words. Occasionally <i>ou</i> may also represent other vowels – <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʌ/</span> as in <i>trouble</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> as in <i>soul</i>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʊ/</span> as in <i>would</i>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> as in <i>group</i>. The <i>ou</i> in <i>out</i> originally represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span>, as in French, but its pronunciation has changed as part of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Vowel_Shift" title="Great Vowel Shift">Great Vowel Shift</a>.</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> ⟨ou⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʌu/</span> in the Netherlands or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> in Flanders. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[uː]</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[u]</span>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">[ʊ]</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-13"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-12"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-14"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-16"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, it represents the <a href="/wiki/Vowel" title="Vowel">vowel</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span>, as in <i>vous</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/vu/</span> "you", or the <a href="/wiki/Approximant_consonant" title="Approximant consonant">approximant consonant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span>, as in <i>oui</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wi/</span> "yes".</p>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> this digraph stands for the <a href="/wiki/Close-mid_back_rounded_vowel" title="Close-mid back rounded vowel">close-mid back rounded vowel</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> or for the falling <a href="/wiki/Diphthong" title="Diphthong">diphthong</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ou/</span>, according to dialect.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oû</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write the vowel sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> before what had historically been an <i>s</i>, as in <i>soûl</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sul/</span> "drunk".</p>
<p>⟨<b>ow</b>⟩, in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, usually represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/aʊ/</span> sound as in <i>coward</i>, <i>sundowner</i>, and <i>now</i> or the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span> sound, as in <i>froward</i>, <i>landowner</i>, and <i>know</i>. An exceptional pronunciation is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɒ/</span> in <i>knowledge</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Rowlock" title="Rowlock">rowlock</a></i>. There are many English <a href="/wiki/Heteronym_(linguistics)" title="Heteronym (linguistics)">heteronyms</a> distinguished only by the pronunciation of this digraph, like: <i>bow</i> (front of ship or weapon), <i>bower</i> (a dwelling or string player), <i>lower</i> (to frown or drop), <i>mow</i> (to grimace or cut), <i>row</i> (a dispute or line-up), <i>shower</i> (rain or presenter), <i>sow</i> (a pig or to seed), <i>tower</i> (a building or towboat). In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, this represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔʊ/</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-17"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-14"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-13"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-15"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup> before vowels, it can also represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-15"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-14"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-16"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-18"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ôw</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Kernowek_Standard" title="Kernowek Standard">Kernowek Standard</a> orthography of <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> to refer to a sound that can be either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛʊ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oʊ/</span>. This distribution can also be written ⟨êw⟩.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-16"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>oy</b>⟩ is found in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, oy represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔɪ/</span>. Examples in English include <i>toy</i> and <i>annoy</i>. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/oɪ/<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-17"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-15"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-17"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup>~/ɔɪ/<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-19"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></span>; in the words <i>oy</i> ('egg') and <i>moy</i> ('much'), it can also be pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uɪ/<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-18"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-16"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-18"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup>~/ʊɪ/<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-20"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>oŷ</b>⟩ is an obsolete digraph once used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>øy</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/øʏ/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="P">P</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: P">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>pf</b>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> represents a labial affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pf/</span>. It can be initial (<i>Pferd</i>, 'horse'), medial (<i>Apfel</i>, 'apple'), or final (<i>Knopf</i>, 'button'). Where it appears in English, usually in names or words recently derived from German, it is ordinarily simplified to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ph</b>⟩, in English and some other languages, represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>, mostly in words derived from <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>. The Ancient Greek letter <a href="/wiki/Phi" title="Phi">phi</a> ⟨Φ, φ⟩ originally represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʰ/</span> (an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">aspirated</a> <i>p</i> sound), and was thus transcribed into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_orthography" title="Latin orthography">Latin orthography</a> as ⟨PH⟩, a convention that was transferred to some other Western European languages. The Greek pronunciation of ⟨φ⟩ later changed to /f/, and this was also the sound adopted in other languages for the relevant loanwords. Exceptionally, in English, ⟨ph⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/v/</span> in the name <i><a href="/wiki/Stephen" title="Stephen">Stephen</a></i> and some speakers' pronunciations of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nephew" title="Nephew">nephew</a></i>.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> languages (and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_auxiliary_languages" title="International auxiliary languages">international auxiliary languages</a> <a href="/wiki/Interlingua" title="Interlingua">Interlingua</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occidental_language" title="Occidental language">Occidental</a>) also use ⟨ph⟩ for Greek loanwords. In German it can be replaced by ⟨f⟩; the replacement is allowed in certain cases according to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_spelling_reform_of_1996" title="German spelling reform of 1996">German spelling reform of 1996</a>. In most Romance (such as <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>) and Germanic (such as Dutch and Swedish) languages, ⟨f⟩ is used rather than ⟨ph⟩. Languages written in a Cyrillic script, such as Russian, Ukrainian, and Bulgarian, regularly use ⟨Ф, ф⟩, similar to the Greek ⟨Φ, φ⟩. In <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>, ⟨ph⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span> in native words, but only word-initially as the result of an initial <a href="/wiki/Consonant_mutation" title="Consonant mutation">consonant mutation</a> of a word beginning with ⟨p⟩. <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a> uses ⟨f⟩ for words of Greek origin, while ⟨ph⟩ represents the <a href="/wiki/Lenition" title="Lenition">lenited</a> form of ⟨p⟩, resulting in the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span> as well. In <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, ⟨ph⟩ is used exclusively for /f/; there is no letter ⟨f⟩ in the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">Vietnamese alphabet</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Old_High_German" title="Old High German">Old High German</a>, ⟨ph⟩ stands for the <a href="/wiki/Affricate_consonant" title="Affricate consonant">affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pf/</span>. In romanizations of <a href="/wiki/Indo-Aryan_languages" title="Indo-Aryan languages">Indo-Aryan languages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">Thai</a> and <a href="/wiki/Khmer_language" title="Khmer language">Khmer</a>, ⟨ph⟩ represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">aspirated sound</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʰ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet, it was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʼ/</span>. In some non-standard spellings of English, like <a href="/wiki/Leet" title="Leet">leet</a>, ⟨ph⟩ may be used as a replacement of all occurrences of ⟨f⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>pl</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pˡ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>pm</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵖm/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>pn</b>⟩ is used in English for an initial sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/n/</span> in words of Greek origin such as <i>pneumatic.</i> When not initial, it represents the sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pn/</span>, as in <i>apnea.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>pp</b>⟩ is used in romanized <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a> for the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/p͈/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ps</b>⟩ is used in English for an initial sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> in words of Greek origin such as <i>psyche.</i> When not initial, it represents the sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ps/</span>, as in <i>ellipse.</i> It is also used in the <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona language</a> to write a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whistled_sibilant" title="Whistled sibilant">whistled sibilant</a> cluster <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ps͎/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>pt</b>⟩ is used in several languages for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span> in words of Greek origin, where it was <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pt/</span>. An example in English is <i><a href="/wiki/Pterosaur" title="Pterosaur">pterosaur</a></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈtɛrəsɔr/</span>, and an exception is <i>ptarmigan</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'t' in 'tie'">t</span><span title="/ɑːr/ 'ar' in 'far'">ɑːr</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/ɪ/ or /ə/ 'e' in 'roses'">ᵻ</span><span title="'g' in 'guy'">ɡ</span><span title="/ən/ 'on' in 'button'">ən</span></span>/</a></span></span>, which is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gaelic_language" title="Gaelic language">Gaelic</a>, not Greek. When not initial, <i>pt</i> represents the sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pt/</span>, as in <i>apt.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>pw</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pʷ/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Q">Q</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Q">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>qg</b>⟩ is used to write the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǃχ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a>. It was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_click" title="Voiceless alveolar click">voiceless alveolar click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǃ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>qh</b>⟩ is used in various alphabets. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Quechua_languages" title="Quechua languages">Quechua</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʰ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a>, it represents the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǃʰ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>qk</b>⟩ was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_click" title="Voiceless alveolar click">voiceless alveolar click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǃ/</span> (equivalent to ⟨qg⟩).</p>
<p>⟨<b>qo</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kw/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>qq</b>⟩ is used in Haida (Bringhurst orthography) for ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʼ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is the glottalized click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǃˀ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><span id="qu">qu</span></b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_orthography" title="Catalan orthography">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galician</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">Spanish orthographies</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> before the vowel letters <i>e, i</i>, where the letter <i>c</i> represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span> (<a href="/wiki/Castilian_Spanish" title="Castilian Spanish">Castilian Spanish</a> and most of <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">Galicia</a>) or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> (<a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_American_Spanish" title="Latin American Spanish">Latin American Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>). This dates to <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> <i>qu</i>, and ultimately the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Indo-European" title="Proto-Indo-European">Proto-Indo-European</a> <a href="/wiki/Labialized_velar_consonant" title="Labialized velar consonant">labialized velar consonant</a> */kʷ/; in English this sound instead became written primarily as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wh_(digraph)" title="Wh (digraph)"><i>wh</i></a>, due to <a href="/wiki/Grimm%27s_law" title="Grimm's law">Grimm's law</a> changing <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">kʷ</span> &gt; <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">xʷ</span> (written <i>hw</i>), and Middle English spelling change switching <i>hw</i> to <i>wh</i>. In English, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/k/</span> in words derived from those languages (e.g., <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quiche" title="wikt:quiche">quiche</a></i>), and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kw/</span> in other words, including borrowings from Latin (e.g., <i><a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/quantity" title="wikt:quantity">quantity</a></i>). In the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet, it was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʷ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">Vietnamese</a> it was used to represent the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kw/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> sound. In Cornish, it represents the <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kw/</span> sound.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UCRdict_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-UCRdict-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>qv</b>⟩ is used for glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀw/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>qw</b>⟩ is used in some languages for the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/qʷ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_language" title="Mi'kmaq language">Mi'kmaq</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʷ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Kernowek_Standard" title="Kernowek Standard">Kernowek Standard</a> and <a href="/wiki/Standard_Written_Form" title="Standard Written Form">Standard Written Form</a> orthographies for Revived Cornish, and in <a href="/wiki/William_Jordan_(writer)" title="William Jordan (writer)">William Jordan</a>'s 1611 <i>Creation of the World</i>, it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kw/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-19"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-17"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-21"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>qy</b>⟩ is used for glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀj/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="R">R</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: R">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>rd</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a> for a retroflex stop, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʈ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rh</b>⟩ is found in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> with words from the <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Transliteration" title="Transliteration">transliterated</a> through the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin language</a>. Examples include "rhapsody", "rhetoric" and "rhythm". These were pronounced in Ancient Greek with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless" title="Voiceless">voiceless</a> "r" sound, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r̥/</span>, as in <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> ⟨hr⟩. The digraph may also be found within words, but always at the start of a word component, e.g., "polyrhythmic". <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, and the auxiliary language <a href="/wiki/Interlingua" title="Interlingua">Interlingua</a> use <i>rh</i> in the same way. ⟨Rh⟩ is also found in the <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh language</a> where it represents a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless" title="Voiceless">voiceless</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">alveolar trill</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">r̥</span>), that is a voiceless "r" sound. It can be found anywhere; the most common occurrence in the English language from Welsh is in the slightly respelled given name "Rhonda". In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wade-Giles" title="Wade-Giles">Wade-Giles</a> transliteration, ⟨rh⟩ is used for the syllable-final rhotic of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Gwoyeu_Romatzyh" title="Gwoyeu Romatzyh">Gwoyeu Romatzyh</a> romanization of <a href="/wiki/Mandarin_Chinese" title="Mandarin Chinese">Mandarin Chinese</a>, initial <i>rh-</i> indicates an even tone on a syllable beginning in <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʐ/</span>, which is otherwise spelled <i>r-.</i> In <a href="/wiki/Pur%C3%A9pecha_language" title="Purépecha language">Purépecha</a>, it is a <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_flap" title="Retroflex flap">retroflex flap</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɽ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rl</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a> for a retroflex lateral, written <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɭ/</span> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IPA" title="IPA">IPA</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic language</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɬː/</span> as the result of an assimilation of a consonant cluster with a uvular consonant as the first component.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Inuktitut" title="Inuktitut">Inuktitut</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɴm/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rn</b>⟩ represents the retroflex nasal <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɳ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a> (see <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a>). In the <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic language</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɴ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Inuktitut" title="Inuktitut">Inuktitut</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɴn/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rp</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic language</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/pː/</span> as the result of an assimilation of a consonant cluster with a uvular consonant as the first component.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rr</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> for ⟨r⟩, depending on <a href="/wiki/Etymology" title="Etymology">etymology</a>. It normally appears in words of <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> or <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance</a> origin, and "rrh" in words of ancient <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a> origin. It is quite a common digraph, found in words as diverse as <i>arrest</i>, <i>carry</i>, and <i>sorry</i>. Some words with "rr" are relatively recent <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a> from other languages; examples include <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burro" title="Burro">burro</a></i> from <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>. It is often used in impromptu pronunciation guides to denote either an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_tap" title="Alveolar tap">alveolar tap</a> or an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">alveolar trill</a>. It is a letter in the Albanian alphabet.</p>
<p>In several European languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> or <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, "rr" represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_trill" title="Alveolar trill">alveolar trill</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r/</span> (or the <a href="/wiki/Voiced_uvular_fricative" title="Voiced uvular fricative">voiced uvular fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>) and contrasts with the single "r", which represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_tap" title="Alveolar tap">alveolar tap</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɾ/</span> (in Catalan and Spanish a single "r" also represents the alveolar trill at the beginning of words or syllables). In Italian or Finnish, "rr" is furthermore a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Geminate_consonant" title="Geminate consonant">geminate</a> (long) consonant <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rː/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/χ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it can represent either <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/rː/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɾʰ/</span>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɹ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-22"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>rs</b>⟩ was equivalent to ⟨<b>rz</b>⟩ and stood for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r̝/</span> (modern <i>ř</i>) in medieval <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Greenlandic_language" title="Greenlandic language">Greenlandic language</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sː/</span> as the result of an assimilation of a consonant cluster with a uvular consonant as the first component.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rt</b>⟩ is used for Australian Aboriginal languages such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a> for a retroflex stop <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʈ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rw</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɻʷ/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>rz</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Polish_alphabet" title="Polish alphabet">Polish</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kashubian_alphabet" title="Kashubian alphabet">Kashubian</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_retroflex_fricative" title="Voiced retroflex fricative">voiced retroflex fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʐ/</span>, similar to English "zh" as in <i>Zhivago</i>. Examples from Polish are <i><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-marzec.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/41/Pl-marzec.ogg" title="Pl-marzec.ogg">ma<b>rz</b>ec</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Pl-marzec.ogg" title="File:Pl-marzec.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></i> "March" and <i><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-Rzeka.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/9e/Pl-Rzeka.ogg" title="Pl-Rzeka.ogg"><b>rz</b>eka</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo"
