style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Pl-Rzeka.ogg" title="File:Pl-Rzeka.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></i> "river". ⟨Rz⟩ represents the same sound as ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%BB" title="Ż">ż</a>⟩, the only difference being that ⟨ż⟩ evolved from a *g while ⟨rz⟩ is descended from a palatalized ar ( <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">*rʲ</span> ). ⟨Rz⟩ usually corresponds to Czech ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%98" title="Ř">ř</a>⟩, though the pronunciations are different. When preceded by a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" title="Voiceless consonant">voiceless consonant</a> (ch, k, p, t) or <a href="/wiki/Final-obstruent_devoicing" title="Final-obstruent devoicing">end of a word</a>, ⟨rz⟩ devoices to ⟨sz⟩, as in <i><span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap"><a href="/wiki/File:Pl-przed.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></a> </span><a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/b4/Pl-przed.ogg" title="Pl-przed.ogg">p<b>rz</b>ed</a></span> <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">(<a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help"><span style="cursor:help;">help</span></a>·<a href="/wiki/File:Pl-przed.ogg" title="File:Pl-przed.ogg"><span style="cursor:help;">info</span></a>)</small></span></i> "before", pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Polish" title="Help:IPA for Polish">[ˈpʂɛt]</a></span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="S">S</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: S">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>sc</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Italian_orthography" title="Italian orthography">Italian</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃː/</span> before the front vowel letters <i>e, i</i>. It is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> in Catalan, French, English, Occitan and Brazilian Portuguese (e.g. French/English <i>reminiscence</i>, Brazilian Portuguese <i>reminiscência</i>, Catalan <i>reminiscència</i>, Occitan <i>reminiscéncia</i>). In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Old_English_orthography" title="Old English orthography">Old English</a> it usually represented <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sç</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> in a few verb forms such as simple past <i>acquiesça</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/akjɛsa/</span>. It is also used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Brazilian Portuguese</a> as in the imperative form of verbs ending with <i>scer</i>: <i>crescer</i> <i>cresça</i>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sg</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Sh_(digraph)" title="Sh (digraph)">sh</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages. In English, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>. See <a href="/wiki/Sh_(digraph)" title="Sh (digraph)">separate article</a>. See also <b>ſh</b> <a href="#Other_letters">below</a>, which has the capitalized forms SH and ŞH.</p>
<p>⟨<b>si</b>⟩ is used in English for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span> in words such as <i>fusion</i> (see <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yod-coalescence" title="Yod-coalescence">yod-coalescence</a>). In <a href="/wiki/Polish_orthography" title="Polish orthography">Polish orthography</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɕ/</span> whenever it precedes a vowel, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɕi/</span> whenever it precedes a consonant (or in the end of the word), and is considered a graphic variant of <a href="/wiki/%C5%9A" title="Ś">ś</a> appearing in other situations.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sj</b>⟩ is used <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> to write the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal-velar_fricative" title="Voiceless palatal-velar fricative"><i>sje</i> sound</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɧ/</span> (see also ⟨sk⟩) and in <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Danish_language" title="Danish language">Danish</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> to write <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">Voiceless postalveolar fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sk</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> to write the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal-velar_fricative" title="Voiceless palatal-velar fricative"><i>sje</i> sound</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɧ/</span>. It takes by rule this sound value before the front vowels (<i>e, i, y, ä</i> and <i>ö</i>) word or root initially (as in <i>sked</i> (spoon)), while normally representing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sk/</span> in other positions. In Norwegian and Faroese, it is used to write <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiceless postalveolar fricative">voiceless postalveolar fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> (only in front of <i>i</i>, <i>y</i>, <i>ei</i> and <i>øy</i>/<i>oy</i>).</p>
<p>⟨<b>sl</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Iraqw_language" title="Iraqw language">Iraqw</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei languages</a> to write the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lateral_fricative" title="Lateral fricative">lateral fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɬ/</span>. <i>(Sl</i> is used in the French tradition to transcribe <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɬ/</span> in other languages as well, as in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a>.)</p>
<p>⟨<b>sp</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃp/</span> as in <i>Spaß</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃpaːs/</span> instead of using schp (or chp).</p>
<p>⟨<b>sr</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Kosraean_language" title="Kosraean language">Kosraean</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʂ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ss</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>. For its use in the Wade–Giles system of Romanization of Chinese, see <a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles#Empty_rime" title="Wade–Giles">Wade–Giles → Empty rime</a>. In other languages, such as <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-23"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">Italian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">Occitan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a>, where ⟨<b>s</b>⟩ transcribes <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span> between vowels (and elsewhere in the case of Yup'ik), ⟨<b>ss</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span> in that position (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sː/</span> in Italian and also in some cases in Cornish<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-24"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup>). In romanized <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, it represents the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s͈/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>st</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃt/</span> as in <i>Stadt</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃtat/</span> instead of using scht (or cht). In some parts of northern Germany, the pronunciation <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/st/</span> (as in English) is still quite common in the local dialect.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sv</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona language</a> to write the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whistled_sibilant" title="Whistled sibilant">whistled sibilant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s͎/</span>. This was written <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C8%BF" title="ȿ">ȿ</a> from 1931 to 1955.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sx</b>⟩ in used in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sʔ/</span>, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-convention" title="X-convention">Esperanto</a> as an unofficial surrogate of ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%9C" title="Ŝ">ŝ</a>⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>sy</b>⟩ is used to write the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Malay_language" title="Malay language">Malay</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Sz_(digraph)" title="Sz (digraph)">sz</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages. See article.</p>
<p>⟨<b>s-c</b>⟩ and ⟨<b>s-cc</b>⟩ are used in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> for the sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/stʃ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>s-g</b>⟩ and ⟨<b>s-gg</b>⟩ are used in <a href="/wiki/Piedmontese_language" title="Piedmontese language">Piedmontese</a> for the sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/zdʒ/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="T">T</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: T">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>tc</b>⟩ is used for the palatal click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǂ/</span> in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a>, and to write the affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Sandawe_language" title="Sandawe language">Sandawe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tf</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_dental_affricate" title="Voiceless dental affricate">voiceless dental affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡θ/</span></p>
<p>⟨<b>tg</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tχ/</span> in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_orthography" title="Catalan orthography">Catalan spelling</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʒ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b><a href="/wiki/Th_(digraph)" title="Th (digraph)">th</a></b>⟩ is used in several languages. In English, it can represent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ð/</span>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/θ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span>. See article. See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pronunciation_of_English_th" title="Pronunciation of English th">Pronunciation of English th</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ti</b>⟩, before a vowel, is usually pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sj/</span> in French.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tj</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Norwegian_language" title="Norwegian language">Norwegian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Faroese_language" title="Faroese language">Faroese</a> words like <i><b>tj</b>ære</i>/<i><b>tj</b>øra</i> ('tar') for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ç/</span> (Norwegian) and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> (Faroese). In the closely related <a href="/wiki/Swedish_alphabet" title="Swedish alphabet">Swedish alphabet</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɕ/</span>, as in <i><b>tj</b>ära</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈɕæːɾa/</span>. It is, or was, also used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span> in many Dutch-based orthographies in Indonesia and Surinam. In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a>, it represents a postalveolar stop, written <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ṯ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ḏ/</span>. This sound is also written ⟨dj⟩, ⟨ty⟩, ⟨dy⟩, ⟨c⟩, or ⟨j⟩. In Catalan spelling it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡ʒ/</span></p>
<p>⟨<b>tl</b>⟩ is used in various orthographies for the affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɬ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tł</b>⟩ is used in the transcription of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athabascan_languages" title="Athabascan languages">Athabascan languages</a> for a lateral affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɬ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɬʰ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tm</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nasal_release" title="Nasal release">nasally released</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t̪͡pn̪͡m/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tn</b>⟩ is used for a prestopped nasal <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵗn/</span> in the orthography of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and for the similar <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t̪n̪/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tp</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a> of <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a> for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t̪͡p/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tr</b>⟩ generally represents a sound like a <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_consonant" title="Retroflex consonant">retroflex</a> version of English "ch" in areas of German influence, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Truk_Lagoon" title="Truk Lagoon"><i>Truk</i> lagoon</a>, now spelled ⟨chuuk⟩. For instance, in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Malagasy_language" title="Malagasy language">Malagasy</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʂ/</span>. In southern <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">dialects</a> of <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">Vietnamese</a>, ⟨tr⟩ represents a <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_affricate" title="Voiceless retroflex affricate">voiceless retroflex affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʂ/</span>. In the northern dialects, this sound is pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɕ/</span>, just like what ⟨ch⟩ represents. ⟨Tr⟩ was formerly considered a distinct letter of the <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_alphabet" title="Vietnamese alphabet">Vietnamese alphabet</a>, but today is not.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ts</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Basque_alphabet" title="Basque alphabet">Basque</a>, where it represents an <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">apical</a> <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar affricate">voiceless alveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t̺s̺/</span>. It contrasts with ⟨tz⟩, which is <a href="/wiki/Laminal_consonant" title="Laminal consonant">laminal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t̻s̻/</span>. In the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Hausa_language" title="Hausa language">Hausa</a>, ⟨ts⟩ represents an alveolar ejective fricative <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sʼ/</span> or affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tsʼ/</span>), depending on dialect. It is considered a distinct letter, and placed between ⟨t⟩ and ⟨u⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>. It is also used in the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_orthography" title="Catalan orthography">Catalan spelling</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡s/</span></p>
<p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wade-Giles" title="Wade-Giles">Wade-Giles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Mandarin" title="Yale romanization of Mandarin">Yale</a> romanizations of <a href="/wiki/Chinese_language" title="Chinese language">Chinese</a> use ⟨ts⟩ for an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">unaspirated</a> <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar affricate">voiceless alveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ts/</span>. Wade-Giles also uses ⟨ts'⟩ for the aspirated equivalent <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tsʰ/</span>. These are equivalent to <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> ⟨z⟩ and ⟨c⟩, respectively. The <a href="/wiki/Hepburn_romanization" title="Hepburn romanization">Hepburn romanization</a> of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">Japanese</a> uses ⟨ts⟩ for a <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar affricate">voiceless alveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ts/</span>). In native Japanese words, this sound only occurs before ⟨u⟩, but it may occur before other vowels in <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a>. Other romanization systems write <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tsu/</span> as ⟨tu⟩. ⟨Ts⟩ in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">Tagalog</a> is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>. The sequence ⟨ts⟩ occurs in English, but it has no special function and simply represents a sequence of ⟨t⟩ and ⟨s⟩. It occurs word-initially only in some <a href="/wiki/Loanword" title="Loanword">loanwords</a>, such as <i><a href="/wiki/Tsunami" title="Tsunami">tsunami</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Tsar" title="Tsar">tsar</a></i>. Most English-speakers do not pronounce a <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t/</span> in such words and pronounce them as if they were spelled ⟨sunami⟩ and ⟨sar⟩, respectively.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ts̃</b>⟩ was used in the orthography of medieval <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless postalveolar affricate">voiceless postalveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ʃ/</span>; this is now represented by ⟨tx⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tt</b>⟩ is used in the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/c/</span>, and in romanized <a href="/wiki/Kabyle_language" title="Kabyle language">Kabyle</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ts/</span>. In romanized <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">Korean</a>, it represents the fortis sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͈/</span>, and in Haida (Bringhurst orthography) it is ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʼ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tw</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʷ/</span> in the orthography of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>tx</b>⟩ is used in the orthographies of <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, as well as some indigenous languages of <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, for a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_postalveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless postalveolar affricate">voiceless postalveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡ʃ/</span>. In the orthography of <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> it represents a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʔ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ty</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_alphabet" title="Hungarian alphabet">Hungarian alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/cç/</span>, a <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_affricate" title="Voiceless palatal affricate">voiceless palatal affricate</a>; in Hungarian, digraphs are considered single letters, and <a href="/wiki/Acronym" title="Acronym">acronyms</a> keep them intact. In the orthography of Xhosa, ⟨ty⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʲʼ/</span>. In that of <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃk/</span>. In the orthography of Tagalog it uses <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʃ/</span>. In the <a href="/wiki/Transcription_of_Australian_Aboriginal_languages" title="Transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages">transcription of Australian Aboriginal languages</a> such as <a href="/wiki/Warlpiri_language" title="Warlpiri language">Warlpiri</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitjantjatjara_language" title="Pitjantjatjara language">Pitjantjatjara</a>, it represents a postalveolar stop, either voiceless <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ṯ/</span> or voiced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ḏ/</span>. (This sound is also written ⟨tj⟩, ⟨dj⟩, ⟨dy⟩, ⟨c⟩, and ⟨j⟩).</p>
<p>⟨<b>tz</b>⟩ is used in the orthographies of <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolar_affricate" title="Voiceless alveolar affricate">voiceless alveolar affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/t͡s/</span>). In Basque, this sound is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Laminal" title="Laminal">laminal</a> and contrasts with the <a href="/wiki/Apical_consonant" title="Apical consonant">apical</a> affricate represented by ⟨ts⟩. It is also used in Catalan to represent the voiced alveolar affricate <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/d͡z/</span>. For its use in the Wade–Giles system of Romanization of Chinese, see <a href="/wiki/Wade%E2%80%93Giles#Empty_rime" title="Wade–Giles">Wade–Giles → Empty rime</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="U">U</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: U">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>u′</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> or <a href="/wiki/Creaky_voice" title="Creaky voice">creaky</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ṵ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uc</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">Nahuatl</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʷ/</span> before a consonant. Before a vowel, ⟨cu⟩ is used.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ue</b>⟩ is found in many <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">languages</a>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, ⟨ue⟩ represents /ju/ or /u/ as in <i>cue</i> or <i>true</i>, respectively. In <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, it is equivalent to <a href="/wiki/%C3%9C" title="Ü">Ü</a>, and as such may appear in proper names of people, representing <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʏ/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/yː/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ug</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɣʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uh</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the breathy or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breathy_voice" title="Breathy voice">murmured</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ṳ/</span>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nahuatl_language" title="Nahuatl language">Nahuatl</a>, it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> before a consonant. Before a vowel, ⟨hu⟩ is used.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ui</b>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> stands for the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œy/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/</span> after a <a href="/wiki/Velarization" title="Velarization">velarized</a> (broad) consonant, and in Irish, it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪ/ /ʊ/ /iː/ /uː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant. In <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a>, it represents the diphthong <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʊɪ̯/</span>, which appears only in <a href="/wiki/Interjection" title="Interjection">interjections</a> such as <i>"pf<b>ui</b>!"</i>. In <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>, it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> in <i>fruit</i>, <i>juice</i>, <i>suit</i> and <i>pursuit</i>. However, in many English words, this does not hold. For example, it fails in words where the <i>u</i> in <i>ui</i> functions as a modifier of a preceding <i>g</i> (forcing <i>g</i> to remain <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ/</span> rather than shifting to <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span> in <i>guild</i>, <i>guilt</i>, <i>guilty</i>, <i>sanguine</i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Guinea" title="Guinea">Guinea</a></i>, etc.), doing the same with <i>c</i> (in words like <i>circuit</i> and <i>biscuit</i>), or in cases of unusual etymological spelling or syllable separation (e.g. <i>build</i>, <i>suite</i>, and <i>intuition</i>). In Mandarin <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wei̯/</span> after a consonant. (In initial position, this is spelled <i>wei.</i>) In <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, it is not a digraph, but a predictable sequence <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɥi/</span>, as in <i>h</i>ui<i>t</i> "eight".</p>
<p>⟨<b>uí</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>úi</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Irish_orthography" title="Irish orthography">Irish</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span> between a broad and a slender consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>um</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ũ/</span>, and in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œ̃/</span> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œm/</span> before a vowel).</p>
<p>⟨<b>úm</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ũ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>un</b>⟩ is used in many languages to write a <a href="/wiki/Nasal_vowel" title="Nasal vowel">nasal vowel</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> before a consonant, and in many <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> languages, it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ũ/</span>, while in French it is <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œ̃/</span>, or among the younger generation <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u̯ən/</span> is spelled <i>un</i> after a consonant, <i>wen</i> initially.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ún</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">Portuguese orthography</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ũ/</span> before a consonant.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ün</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tibetan_Pinyin" title="Tibetan Pinyin">Tibetan Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ỹ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uŋ</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lakhota_language" title="Lakhota language">Lakhota</a> for the nasal vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ũ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uo</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> to write the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/o/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>, where <i>o</i> stands for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uq</b>⟩, in the practical orthography of the <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">Taa language</a>, represents the <a href="/wiki/Pharyngealization" title="Pharyngealization">pharyngealized</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uˤ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ur</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʁʷ/</span>, and in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> to write the <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">trilled</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʙ̝/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uu</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/y/</span>. In languages with phonemic long vowels, it may be used to write <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/uː/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>uw</b>⟩ occurs in <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a>, as in ⟨<b>uw</b>⟩ (<i>yours</i>), d<b>uw</b>en (<i>to push</i>) . It is used in <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iʊ/</span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-20"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-18"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-19"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-25"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/yʊ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-26"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>ux</b>⟩ is used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X-convention" title="X-convention">Esperanto</a> as an unofficial surrogate of ⟨<a href="/wiki/%C5%AC" title="Ŭ">ŭ</a>⟩.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="V">V</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: V">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>vb</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Labiodental_flap" title="Labiodental flap">labiodental flap</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ⱱ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>vg</b>⟩ was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_click" title="Voiceless palatal click">voiceless palatal click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǂ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>vh</b>⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/v/</span> in the <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona language</a>. It was also used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Aspirated_consonant" title="Aspirated consonant">aspirated</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Palatal_click" title="Palatal click">palatal click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǂʰ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>vk</b>⟩ was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_click" title="Voiceless palatal click">voiceless palatal click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǂ/</span> (equivalent to ⟨vg⟩).</p>
<p>⟨<b>vn</b>⟩ was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Palatal_nasal_click" title="Palatal nasal click">palatal nasal click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǂ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>vv</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Central_Alaskan_Yup%27ik_language" title="Central Alaskan Yup'ik language">Central Alaskan Yup'ik</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="W">W</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: W">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b><span id="wh">wh</span></b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_orthography" title="English orthography">English</a> to represent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic" title="Proto-Germanic">Proto-Germanic</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hw/</span>, the continuation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PIE" title="PIE">PIE</a> <a href="/wiki/Labialized_velar_consonant" title="Labialized velar consonant">labiovelar</a> <span class="Unicode" lang="ine" style="white-space: nowrap" title="Proto-Indo-European language" xml:lang="ine">*/kʷ/</span> (which became ⟨<a href="#qu">qu</a>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">Latin</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Romance_languages" title="Romance languages">Romance languages</a>). Most English question words begin with this digraph, hence the terms <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wh-word" title="Wh-word">wh-word</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wh-question" title="Wh-question">wh-question</a></i>. The spelling changed from ⟨<a href="#hw">hw</a>⟩ to ⟨wh⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Middle_English" title="Middle English">Middle English</a>. In most dialects it is now pronounced <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span>, but some (especially in <a href="/wiki/Scottish_English" title="Scottish English">Scotland</a>) retain the distinct pronunciation /hw/, realized as a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_labio-velar_approximant" title="Voiceless labio-velar approximant">voiceless w sound</a>. In a few words (<i>who</i>, <i>whole</i>, etc.) the pronunciation is /h/. For details, see <a href="/wiki/Pronunciation_of_English_%E2%9F%A8wh%E2%9F%A9" title="Pronunciation of English ⟨wh⟩">Pronunciation of English ⟨wh⟩</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_language" title="Māori language">Māori language</a>, ⟨wh⟩ represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɸ/</span> or more commonly <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/f/</span>, with some regional variations approaching <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/hw/</span>. In the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taranaki_Region" title="Taranaki Region">Taranaki</a> region, for some speakers, this represents a glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wʼ/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w̤/</span>, a murmured variant of <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/w/</span> found in loan words. In <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a>, it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʍ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-21"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-19"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-27"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>wr</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> for words which formerly began <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/wr/</span>, now <a href="/wiki/Phonological_history_of_English_consonant_clusters#wr" title="Phonological history of English consonant clusters">reduced to /r/</a> in virtually all dialects.</p>
<p>⟨<b>wu</b>⟩ is used in Mandarin <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a> to write the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/u/</span> in initial position, as in the name <i><a href="/wiki/Wuhan" title="Wuhan">Wuhan</a>.</i> It is sometimes found with this value in Romanized Korean as well, as in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanwu" title="Hanwu">hanwu</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ww</b>⟩ is used in Haida (Bringhurst orthography) for glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀw/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>wx</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀw/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="X">X</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: X">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>xf</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the supposed fricative <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/x͡ɸ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>xg</b>⟩ is used to write the click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǁχ/</span> in <a href="/wiki/Naro_language" title="Naro language">Naro</a>. It was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_lateral_click" title="Voiceless lateral click">voiceless lateral click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǁ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>xh</b>⟩, in <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a>, represents the sound of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_affricate" title="Voiced postalveolar affricate">voiced postalveolar affricate</a> consonant <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>, as in the surname <i>Hoxha</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈhɔdʒa/</span>. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pashto_language" title="Pashto language">Pashto</a> too it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dʒ/</span>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In <a href="/wiki/Zulu_language" title="Zulu language">Zulu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> it represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aspiration_(phonetics)" title="Aspiration (phonetics)">voiceless aspirated</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolar_lateral_click" title="Alveolar lateral click">alveolar lateral click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kǁʰ/</span>, for example in the name of the language <i><a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a></i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˈkǁʰoːsa/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Walloon_language" title="Walloon language">Walloon</a> to write a sound that is variously <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>, depending on the dialect. In Canadian <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_language" title="Tlingit language">Tlingit</a> it represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/χ/</span>, which in Alaska is written <i>x̱.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>xi</b>⟩ is used in English for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/kʃ/</span> in words such as <i>flexion</i>. (It is equivalent to ⟨c⟩ plus the digraph ⟨ti⟩, as in <i>action</i>.)</p>
<p>⟨<b>xk</b>⟩ was used in the Tindall orthography of <a href="/wiki/Khoekhoe_language" title="Khoekhoe language">Khoekhoe</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_lateral_click" title="Voiceless lateral click">voiceless lateral click</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ǁ/</span> (equivalent to ⟨xg⟩).</p>
<p>⟨<b>xö</b>⟩ is used as a letter of the <a href="/wiki/Seri_language" title="Seri language">Seri</a> alphabet, where it represents a <a href="/wiki/Labialization" title="Labialization">labialized</a> <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_uvular_fricative" title="Voiceless uvular fricative">uvular fricative</a>, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/χʷ/</span>. It is placed between <a href="/wiki/X" title="X">X</a> and <a href="/wiki/Y" title="Y">Y</a> in <a href="/wiki/Alphabetical_order" title="Alphabetical order">alphabetical order</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>xu</b>⟩ was used in the <a href="/wiki/Ossetian_language" title="Ossetian language">Ossete</a> Latin alphabet for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/χʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>xw</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_language" title="Tlingit language">Tlingit language</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/xʷ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>x̱w</b>⟩ is used in Alaskan <a href="/wiki/Tlingit_language" title="Tlingit language">Tlingit</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/χʷ/</span>, which in Canada is written <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Xhw_(trigraph)" title="Xhw (trigraph)">xhw</a>.</i></p>
<p>⟨<b>xx</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> for the glottalized click <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑǁˀ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>xy</b>⟩ <span id="xy"></span> is used in the <a href="/wiki/Romanized_Popular_Alphabet" title="Romanized Popular Alphabet">Romanized Popular Alphabet</a> used to write <a href="/wiki/Hmong_language" title="Hmong language">Hmong</a>, where it represents the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ç/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Y">Y</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Y">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>ye</b>⟩ used in various languages. In some languages such as English its used as an <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛi/</span> such as in b<b>ye</b>. In most languages, its used as an <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jɛ/</span> sound. Such as in <b>Ye</b>llow.</p>
<p>⟨<b>yh</b>⟩ was used in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthography_for_languages_of_Guinea_(pre-1985)" title="Orthography for languages of Guinea (pre-1985)">pre-1985 orthography of Guinea</a>, for the "ejective y" or <a href="/wiki/Palatalization_(sound_change)" title="Palatalization (sound change)">palatalized</a> <a href="/wiki/Glottal_stop" title="Glottal stop">glottal stop</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʔʲ/</span>) in <a href="/wiki/Pular_language" title="Pular language">Pular</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Fula_language" title="Fula language">Fula language</a>). In the current orthography it is now written <b><a href="/wiki/%C6%B3" title="Ƴ">ƴ</a></b>. In <a href="/wiki/Xhosa_language" title="Xhosa language">Xhosa</a> it is used for the sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ j̈ /</span>. In a handful of Australian languages, it represents a "dental semivowel".<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (April 2009)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>yi</b>⟩ is used in Mandarin <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a> to write the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/i/</span> when it forms an entire syllable.</p>
<p>⟨<b>yk</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Yanyuwa_language" title="Yanyuwa language">Yanyuwa</a> for a pre-<a href="/wiki/Velar_consonant" title="Velar consonant">velar</a> stop, <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɡ̟ ~ k̟/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ym</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write the vowel sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/im/</span> before another vowel), as in <i>thym</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tɛ̃/</span> "thyme".</p>
<p>⟨<b>yn</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> to write the vowel sound <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span> in some words of Greek origin, such as <i>syncope</i> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/sɛ̃kɔp/</span> "syncope".</p>
<p>⟨<b>yr</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> to write the <a href="/wiki/Trill_consonant" title="Trill consonant">trilled</a> vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/r̝/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>yu</b>⟩ is used in romanized Chinese to write the vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/y/</span>. In Mandarin <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/y/</span> in initial position, whereas in Cantonese <a href="/wiki/Jyutping" title="Jyutping">Jyutping</a> it is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/y/</span> in non-initial position. (See <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jyu_(trigraph)" title="Jyu (trigraph)">jyu</a>.)</p>
<p>⟨<b>yw</b>⟩ is used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/jʷ/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrernte_language#Orthography" title="Arrernte language">Arrernte</a> and for <a href="/wiki/Double_articulation" title="Double articulation">doubly articulated</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɥ/</span> in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Y%C3%A9l%C3%AE_Dnye_language" title="Yélî Dnye language">Yélî Dnye</a>. It is used in <a href="/wiki/Cornish_language" title="Cornish language">Cornish</a> for the diphthongs <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/iʊ/</span>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-KS_1-22"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-KS-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-T_3-20"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-T-3">[3]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SAT-SWF-M_4-20"><a href="#cite_note-SAT-SWF-M-4">[4]</a></sup> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɪʊ/</span>, or <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛʊ/</span>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWF_5-28"><a href="#cite_note-SWF-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>⟨<b>yx</b>⟩ in used in <a href="/wiki/Nambikwara_language" title="Nambikwara language">Nambikwara</a> for a <a href="/wiki/Glottalization" title="Glottalization">glottalized</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀj/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>yy</b>⟩ is used in some languages such as <a href="/wiki/Finnish_language" title="Finnish language">Finnish</a> to write the long vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/yː/</span>. In Haida (Bringhurst orthography) it is glottalized <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ˀj/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Z">Z</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Z">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>zh</b>⟩ represents the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">voiced postalveolar fricative</a> (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span>), like the ⟨s⟩ in <i>pleasure</i>, in <a href="/wiki/Albanian_language" title="Albanian language">Albanian</a> and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Native_American_languages" title="Native American languages">Native American</a> orthographies such as <a href="/wiki/Navajo_language" title="Navajo language">Navajo</a>. It is used for the same sound in some English-language dictionaries, as well as to transliterate the sound when represented by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cyrillic" title="Cyrillic">Cyrillic</a> ⟨ж⟩ and <a href="/wiki/Persian_alphabet" title="Persian alphabet">Persian</a> ⟨ژ⟩ into English; though it is rarely used for this sound in native English words (perhaps the only one being <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/zhoosh" title="wikt:zhoosh"><i>zhoosh</i></a>). ⟨Zh⟩ as a digraph is rare in European languages using the <a href="/wiki/Latin_alphabet" title="Latin alphabet">Latin alphabet</a>; in addition to Albanian it is found in <a href="/wiki/Breton_language" title="Breton language">Breton</a> in words that are pronounced with <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z/</span> in some dialects and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/h/</span> in others. In <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hanyu_Pinyin" title="Hanyu Pinyin">Hanyu Pinyin</a>, ⟨zh⟩ represents the <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_retroflex_affricate" title="Voiceless retroflex affricate">voiceless retroflex affricate</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tʂ/</span>. When the <a href="/wiki/Tamil_language" title="Tamil language">Tamil language</a> is transliterated into the Latin script, ⟨zh⟩ represents a <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_approximant" title="Retroflex approximant">retroflex approximant</a> (Tamil ழ U+0BB4, ḻ, [ɹ]).</p>
<p>⟨<b>zi</b>⟩ in <a href="/wiki/Polish_orthography" title="Polish orthography">Polish orthography</a> represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʑ/</span> whenever it precedes a vowel, and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʑi/</span> whenever it precedes a consonant (or in the end of the word), and is considered a graphic variant of <a href="/wiki/%C5%B9" title="Ź">ź</a> appearing in other situations.</p>
<p>⟨<b>zl</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_lateral_fricative" title="Voiced lateral fricative">voiced lateral fricative</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɮ/</span></p>
<p>⟨<b>zm</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Hebrew_language" title="Hebrew language">Hebrew language</a> as a translation to the latin alphabet. (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/zʔm/</span>)</p>
<p>⟨<b>zr</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʐ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>zs</b>⟩ is the last (forty-fourth) letter of the <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_alphabet" title="Hungarian alphabet">Hungarian alphabet</a>. Its name is "zsé" and represents <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʒ/</span>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_postalveolar_fricative" title="Voiced postalveolar fricative">voiced postalveolar fricative</a>, similar to <i>J</i> in <i>Jacques</i> and <i>s</i> in <i>vision</i>. A few examples are <i>rózsa</i> "rose" and <i>zsír</i> "fat".</p>
<p>⟨<b>zv</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Shona_language" title="Shona language">Shona language</a> to write the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whistled_sibilant" title="Whistled sibilant">whistled sibilant</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/z͎/</span>. This was written <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C9%80" title="ɀ">ɀ</a> from 1931 to 1955.</p>
<p>⟨<b>zw</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch language</a> It represent as a (<span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/zʷ/</span>).</p>
<p>⟨<b>zz</b>⟩ is used in <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">Pinyin</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/dz/</span> in languages such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yi_language" title="Yi language">Yi</a>. It is also used with that value in romanized <a href="/wiki/Kabyle_language" title="Kabyle language">Kabyle</a>. In medieval <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">Czech</a>, it stood for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/s/</span>. In <a href="/wiki/Hadza_language" title="Hadza language">Hadza</a> it is ejective <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/tsʼ/</span>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other">Other <span id="Other_letters"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_Latin-script_digraphs&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Other">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>⟨<b>ɛn</b>⟩, capital ⟨<b>Ɛn</b>⟩, is used in many <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> languages for the nasal vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɛ̃/</span>. <i>Ɛ</i> is an "<a href="/wiki/Latin_epsilon" title="Latin epsilon">open e</a>".</p>
<p>⟨<b>ɔn</b>⟩, capital ⟨<b>Ɔn</b>⟩, is used in many <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">West African</a> languages for the nasal vowel <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ɔ̃/</span>. <i>Ɔ</i> is an "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Open_o" title="Open o">open o</a>".</p>
<p>⟨<b>œu</b>⟩, capitalized ⟨<b>Œu</b>⟩, is used in <a href="/wiki/French_orthography" title="French orthography">French</a> for the vowels <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/œ/</span> and <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ø/</span>. The first element of the digraph, <i><a href="/wiki/%C5%92" title="Œ">œ</a></i>, is itself is a ligature of <i>o</i> and <i>e</i>, and ⟨œu⟩ may also be written as the <a href="/wiki/Trigraph_(orthography)" title="Trigraph (orthography)">trigraph</a> ⟨oeu⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ŋg</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑɡ/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ŋk</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ᵑk/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ŋm</b>⟩ is used in the <a href="/wiki/General_Alphabet_of_Cameroon_Languages" title="General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages">General Alphabet of Cameroon Languages</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Labial-velar_nasal" title="Labial-velar nasal">labial-velar nasal</a> <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋ͡m/</span>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ŋv</b>⟩, capitalized ⟨<b>Ŋv</b>⟩, was used for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ŋʷ/</span> in the old orthography of <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">Zhuang</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bouyei_language" title="Bouyei language">Bouyei</a>; this is now spelled with the <a href="/wiki/Trigraph_(orthography)" title="Trigraph (orthography)">trigraph</a> ⟨ngv⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ſh</b>⟩, capitalized ⟨<b>SH</b>⟩ or sometimes ⟨<b>ŞH</b>⟩, was a digraph used in the Slovene <a href="/wiki/Bohori%C4%8D_alphabet" title="Bohorič alphabet">Bohorič alphabet</a> for <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">/ʃ/</span>. The first element, ⟨ſ⟩, the <a href="/wiki/Long_s" title="Long s">long s</a>, is an archaic non-final form of the letter ⟨s⟩.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ǀg</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǁg</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǃg</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǂg</b>⟩ are used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a> for its four tenuis <a href="/wiki/Click_consonant" title="Click consonant">clicks</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ǀh</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǁh</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǃh</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǂh</b>⟩ are used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a> for its four aspirated <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_click" title="Nasal click">nasal clicks</a>.</p>
<p>⟨<b>ǀn</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǁn</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǃn</b>⟩ ⟨<b>ǂn</b>⟩ are used in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nama_language" title="Nama language">Nama</a> for its four plain nasal clicks.</p>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-9">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation journal"><a class="external text" href="http://www.rifal.org/cahiers_rifal/rifal23.pdf" rel="nofollow">"L'orthographe des langues de la République démocratique du Congo: entre usages et norme"</a> <span style="font-size:85%;">(PDF)</span>. <i>Les cahiers du Rifal</i>. <b>23</b>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+Latin-script+digraphs&amp;rft.atitle=L%99orthographe+des+langues+de+la+R%C3%A9publique+d%C3%A9mocratique+du+Congo%3A+entre+usages+et+norme&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.rifal.org%2Fcahiers_rifal%2Frifal23.pdf&amp;rft.jtitle=Les+cahiers+du+Rifal&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.volume=23"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-GerlyverMeur-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GerlyverMeur_10-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">George, Ken, ed. (September 2009) [First edition published in 1993 under the title <i>Gerlyver Kernewek Kemmyn – An Gerlyver Meur</i>]. "6. Recommended pronunciation". <i>Gerlyver Meur</i> (Second ed.). <a href="/wiki/Kesva_an_Taves_Kernewek" title="Kesva an Taves Kernewek">Cornish Language Board</a>. pp. 28–35. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-1-902917-84-9" title="Special:BookSources/978-1-902917-84-9">978-1-902917-84-9</a>.</cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AList+of+Latin-script+digraphs&amp;rft.atitle=6.+Recommended+pronunciation&amp;rft.btitle=Gerlyver+Meur&amp;rft.date=2009-09&amp;rft.edition=Second&amp;rft.genre=bookitem&amp;rft.isbn=978-1-902917-84-9&amp;rft.pages=28-35&amp;rft.pub=Cornish+Language+Board&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-11">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://www.langsci.ucl.ac.uk/ipa/vowels.html" rel="nofollow">IPA: Vowels</a></span></li>
<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">董峰政, "Taiwanese Tong-iong Pingim Dictionary", 臺南市寧南語言文化協會, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tainan_City" title="Tainan City">Tainan City</a>,Jul 2006.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-UCRdict-13"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-UCRdict_13-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book"><a href="/wiki/Nicholas_Williams" title="Nicholas Williams">Williams, Nicholas</a> (2006).
